The Maturidi Hierarchy of Prophets, Angels, and Humans
Al-Laqqani explains the Maturidi detailed preference hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi detailed classification of superiority among prophets, angelic leaders, common pious humans, and common angels.

Core Idea
The Maturidis distinguish four levels: prophets, angelic leaders, pious humans, and common angels.

Al-Laqqani begins by clarifying a demonstrative pronoun and referencing the outweighed majority view that simply prefers prophets over angels. He then presents the Maturidi nuanced hierarchy, which distinguishes between leaders and commoners within both angels and humans. This detailed view is presented as the preponderant position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview. Notice the reference to the majority view and then the Maturidi distinction.
2
Identify the four categories
The passage mentions four groups: prophets, leaders of angels (ru'asā' al-malā'ika), common pious humans ('awāmm al-bashar al-ṣāliḥīn), and common angels ('awāmm al-malā'ika). Note examples given for each.
Leaders of angels include Jibril and Mika'il; common pious humans include Abu Bakr and Umar; common angels include the Throne-bearers and Cherubim.
3
Understand the hierarchy
The Maturidi view ranks them from highest to lowest: prophets > leaders of angels > common pious humans > common angels.
The text also specifies that sinful humans are not included; angels are superior to sinners.
4
Notice the clarification about sinners
The passage clarifies that 'commoners of humanity' refers to the righteous, not the sinful. This avoids a potential misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (هَذَا) مفعول لمحذوف؛ أي افهم هذا، ويصح غير ذلك كما تقدم في نظيره واسم الإشارة عائد على المذكور من تفضيل الأنبياء على الملائكة، وتفضيل الملائكة على بقية البشر من غير تفصيل كما هو طريقة جمهور المرجوحة، وإنما قدَّمها الناظم؛ لأنه وضع منظومته على مذهبهم. وقوله : (وقَومٌ فَصَّلُوا إِذْ فَضَلُوا أي وقوم من الماتريدية فصلوا بين رؤساء الملائكة وعوامهم وعوام البشر حين فضلوا بين الفريقين، فقالوا : الأنبياء أفضلُ من رؤساء الملائكة ؛ كجبريل وميكائيل، ورؤساء الملائكة أفضل من عوام البشر، وهم أولياؤهم غير الأنبياء؛ كأبي بكر وعمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما، وليس المراد بعوام البشر ما يشمل الفساق فإن الملائكة أفضلُ منهم على الصحيح، وعوام البشر المذكورون أفضل من عوام الملائكة ؛ وهم غير رؤسائهم كحملة العرش؛ وهم أربعة الآن، فإذا كان يوم القيامة أيَّدهم الله بأربعة أخرى قال تعالى: ﴿وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ﴾ [الحاقة: ١٧]؛ لمزيد الجلال عليه يوم القيامة وكالكروبيين بفتح الكاف وتخفيف الراء؛ وهم ملائكة حافون بالعرش، طائفون به، لقبوا بذلك؛ لأنه متصدون للدعاء برفع الكرب عن الأمة، وقيل غير ذلك، وقد علمت أن هذه الطريقة هي الراجحة . فإن قيل : يلزم عليها تفضيل غير المعصوم على المعصوم، أجيب بأن العصمة لا دخل لها في التفضيل، فلا يُنظر لها فيه، وإنما يُنظر للأكثرية في الثواب على العبادة، فعوام البشر أكثر ثواباً من عوام الملائكة لحصول المشقة لعوام البشر في عبادتهم، بخلاف عوام الملائكة، فإن جبلتهم الطاعة، فلا يحصل لهم فيها مشقة. قوله : ( وبعضُ كل بعضه قد يَفضُل) (بعض) بالرفع مبتدأ، و(بعضه) بالنصب مفعول مقدم لـ ( يفضل) الواقع بعده ، والجملة خبر المبتدأ ؛ أي: وبعض كل من الأنبياء والملائكة قد يفضل بعضه الآخر، و(قد) للتحقيق، فبعض الأنبياء كأولي العزم أفضل من بعضهم الآخر، وبعض الملائكة كرؤسائهم أفضل من بعضهم الآخر . وتلخيص ما أشار إليه الناظم أولاً وآخراً مع الجري على الطريقة الراجحة في التفضيل : أن سيدنا محمداً أفضل الخلق على الإطلاق، ويليه سيدنا إبراهيم ثم سيدنا موسى ثم سيدنا عيسى ثم سيدنا نوح، وهؤلاء هم أولو العزم كما تقدَّم، ثم بقية
His saying: 'This' is an object of an omitted verb, meaning 'understand this', and other interpretations are possible as previously mentioned. The demonstrative pronoun refers to what was mentioned concerning the preference of prophets over angels, and the preference of angels over the rest of humanity without distinction, which is the way of the majority of the outweighed group; but the poet presented it because he composed his poem according to their school. And his saying: 'And a group made a distinction when they gave preference' — meaning a group of the Maturidiyya distinguished between the leaders of the angels and their commoners and the commoners of humanity when they gave preference between the two groups. They said: The prophets are superior to the leaders of the angels, like Jibril and Mika'il; and the leaders of the angels are superior to the commoners of humanity, who are their saints other than the prophets, like Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may God be pleased with them both. And by 'commoners of humanity' is not meant those who include the sinful, for indeed angels are superior to them according to the correct view. And the mentioned commoners of humanity are superior to the commoners of the angels, who are other than their leaders, like the bearers of the Throne. They are four now, and on the Day of Resurrection God will strengthen them with four more; He said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be borne above them that day by eight [angels]' [Surah al-Haqqah: 17] — for greater majesty upon Him on the Day of Resurrection. And like the Karubiyyun (Cherubim), with fatha on the kaf and tashdid on the ra? Actually with fatha on the kaf and lightening of the ra? Wait, the text says: 'بفتح الكاف وتخفيف الراء' (with fatha on the kaf and lightening of the ra) — they are angels surrounding the Throne, circling it, so named because they occupy themselves with supplication to remove distress from the nation, and other explanations have been given. And you have known that this way is the most preponderant. Then if it is said: This results in preferring one who is not infallible over one who is infallible, the answer is: Infallibility has no bearing on preference; it is not considered in it. Rather, consideration is given to the greater reward for worship. So the commoners of humanity have more reward than the commoners of the angels because of the hardship incurred by the commoners of humanity in their worship, unlike the commoners of the angels, for obedience is their innate disposition, so they do not experience hardship in it. His saying: 'And some of each may excel some of its other' — 'some' (ba‘ḍ) is in the nominative as subject, and 'its other' (ba‘ḍahu) is in the accusative as an advanced object of 'may excel' (yafḍulu) which follows it, and the sentence is the predicate of the subject. That is: And some of each of the prophets and angels may excel some of its other. And 'may' (qad) is for certainty. So some prophets, like the Messengers of Strong Will, are superior to other prophets, and some angels, like their leaders, are superior to other angels. And the summary of what the poet indicated first and last, while following the preponderant way in preference, is that our master Muhammad is the best of creation absolutely, followed by our master Ibrahim, then our master Musa, then our master 'Isa, then our master Nuh; these are the Messengers of Strong Will as previously mentioned, then the rest...
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining two lines of the poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' concerning the comparison between angels and prophets. The author first clarifies a demonstrative pronoun, then presents the Maturidi detailed view on preference. The Maturidi school distinguishes between leaders of angels (ru'asā') and common angels, and similarly between prophets and common humans (awliyā'). Their hierarchy: Prophets are superior to angelic leaders; angelic leaders are superior to common pious humans (like Abu Bakr and 'Umar); common pious humans are superior to common angels (like the Throne-bearers and Cherubim). The text explains that the common humans referred to are the righteous, not the sinful, as angels are certainly superior to sinners. It then addresses an objection: this preference seems to favor non-infallible humans over infallible angels, but it answers that infallibility is not the criterion—rather, the amount of reward earned through worship matters. Common humans face hardship in worship, earning more reward than common angels who are naturally obedient without effort. The commentary then explains the second line of the poem, which states that within each group, some members may excel others (e.g., the best prophets are the Messengers of Strong Will; the best angels are their leaders). Finally, it summarizes the preponderant view: Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation, followed in order by Ibrahim, Musa, 'Isa, and Nuh, then the rest. The text cuts off mid-sentence at 'then the rest'.

Key Terms
رؤساء الملائكة (ru'asā' al-malā'ika)
عوام البشر ('awāmm al-bashar)
عوام الملائكة ('awāmm al-malā'ika)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe all angels are superior to all humans.
Correction: The Maturidis hold that common pious humans (like Abu Bakr and Umar) are superior to common angels (like Throne-bearers). Only leaders of angels are superior to common pious humans.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi hierarchy, which of the following is correct?
A) Prophets > Leaders of angels > Common pious humans > Common angels
B) Prophets > Common angels > Leaders of angels > Common pious humans
C) Leaders of angels > Prophets > Common pious humans > Common angels
D) Common pious humans > Prophets > Leaders of angels > Common angels

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi view establishes a four-tier hierarchy of superiority: prophets, leaders of angels, common pious humans, and common angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This hierarchy places common pious humans like Abu Bakr and Umar above common angels. Are you striving to be among those pious humans? What specific habit or sin are you clinging to that prevents you from reaching that rank, and when will you begin to change it?
?
If prophets are the highest creation and the leaders of angels serve them, how does that reshape your daily reverence for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him)? Do your actions—such as following his sunna and sending blessings upon him—reflect that belief, or are they perfunctory?
?
The passage states that angels are superior to sinful humans. Do you accept that there is a category of people—sinners—who are lower than angels? Does that thought make you fear for your own state? What one sin will you abandon today to ensure you are not among those who are beneath the angels?

Does Infallibility Determine Superiority?
Al-Laqqani presents an objection and its answer regarding infallibility and preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi response to the objection that preferring non-infallible humans over infallible angels is problematic.

Core Idea
Infallibility is not the measure of preference; reward earned through hardship is.

The Maturidi hierarchy raises a natural objection: how can non-infallible humans be superior to infallible angels? Al-Laqqani presents this objection and answers it by distinguishing the criterion for superiority. The key is not infallibility but the amount of reward (thawāb) from worship, which is greater for humans due to the hardship they face.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully: it claims that the Maturidi ranking implies preferring non-infallible humans over infallible angels, which seems problematic.
2
Read the answer
The answer states that infallibility has no bearing on preference. Instead, the greater reward for worship determines superiority.
3
Understand the reasoning
Humans face hardship in worship, which multiplies reward. Angels are naturally obedient without difficulty, so their reward is less. Thus common pious humans earn more reward than common angels.
This explains why common humans are superior despite lacking infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (هَذَا) مفعول لمحذوف؛ أي افهم هذا، ويصح غير ذلك كما تقدم في نظيره واسم الإشارة عائد على المذكور من تفضيل الأنبياء على الملائكة، وتفضيل الملائكة على بقية البشر من غير تفصيل كما هو طريقة جمهور المرجوحة، وإنما قدَّمها الناظم؛ لأنه وضع منظومته على مذهبهم. وقوله : (وقَومٌ فَصَّلُوا إِذْ فَضَلُوا أي وقوم من الماتريدية فصلوا بين رؤساء الملائكة وعوامهم وعوام البشر حين فضلوا بين الفريقين، فقالوا : الأنبياء أفضلُ من رؤساء الملائكة ؛ كجبريل وميكائيل، ورؤساء الملائكة أفضل من عوام البشر، وهم أولياؤهم غير الأنبياء؛ كأبي بكر وعمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما، وليس المراد بعوام البشر ما يشمل الفساق فإن الملائكة أفضلُ منهم على الصحيح، وعوام البشر المذكورون أفضل من عوام الملائكة ؛ وهم غير رؤسائهم كحملة العرش؛ وهم أربعة الآن، فإذا كان يوم القيامة أيَّدهم الله بأربعة أخرى قال تعالى: ﴿وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ﴾ [الحاقة: ١٧]؛ لمزيد الجلال عليه يوم القيامة وكالكروبيين بفتح الكاف وتخفيف الراء؛ وهم ملائكة حافون بالعرش، طائفون به، لقبوا بذلك؛ لأنه متصدون للدعاء برفع الكرب عن الأمة، وقيل غير ذلك، وقد علمت أن هذه الطريقة هي الراجحة . فإن قيل : يلزم عليها تفضيل غير المعصوم على المعصوم، أجيب بأن العصمة لا دخل لها في التفضيل، فلا يُنظر لها فيه، وإنما يُنظر للأكثرية في الثواب على العبادة، فعوام البشر أكثر ثواباً من عوام الملائكة لحصول المشقة لعوام البشر في عبادتهم، بخلاف عوام الملائكة، فإن جبلتهم الطاعة، فلا يحصل لهم فيها مشقة. قوله : ( وبعضُ كل بعضه قد يَفضُل) (بعض) بالرفع مبتدأ، و(بعضه) بالنصب مفعول مقدم لـ ( يفضل) الواقع بعده ، والجملة خبر المبتدأ ؛ أي: وبعض كل من الأنبياء والملائكة قد يفضل بعضه الآخر، و(قد) للتحقيق، فبعض الأنبياء كأولي العزم أفضل من بعضهم الآخر، وبعض الملائكة كرؤسائهم أفضل من بعضهم الآخر . وتلخيص ما أشار إليه الناظم أولاً وآخراً مع الجري على الطريقة الراجحة في التفضيل : أن سيدنا محمداً أفضل الخلق على الإطلاق، ويليه سيدنا إبراهيم ثم سيدنا موسى ثم سيدنا عيسى ثم سيدنا نوح، وهؤلاء هم أولو العزم كما تقدَّم، ثم بقية
His saying: 'This' is an object of an omitted verb, meaning 'understand this', and other interpretations are possible as previously mentioned. The demonstrative pronoun refers to what was mentioned concerning the preference of prophets over angels, and the preference of angels over the rest of humanity without distinction, which is the way of the majority of the outweighed group; but the poet presented it because he composed his poem according to their school. And his saying: 'And a group made a distinction when they gave preference' — meaning a group of the Maturidiyya distinguished between the leaders of the angels and their commoners and the commoners of humanity when they gave preference between the two groups. They said: The prophets are superior to the leaders of the angels, like Jibril and Mika'il; and the leaders of the angels are superior to the commoners of humanity, who are their saints other than the prophets, like Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may God be pleased with them both. And by 'commoners of humanity' is not meant those who include the sinful, for indeed angels are superior to them according to the correct view. And the mentioned commoners of humanity are superior to the commoners of the angels, who are other than their leaders, like the bearers of the Throne. They are four now, and on the Day of Resurrection God will strengthen them with four more; He said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be borne above them that day by eight [angels]' [Surah al-Haqqah: 17] — for greater majesty upon Him on the Day of Resurrection. And like the Karubiyyun (Cherubim), with fatha on the kaf and tashdid on the ra? Actually with fatha on the kaf and lightening of the ra? Wait, the text says: 'بفتح الكاف وتخفيف الراء' (with fatha on the kaf and lightening of the ra) — they are angels surrounding the Throne, circling it, so named because they occupy themselves with supplication to remove distress from the nation, and other explanations have been given. And you have known that this way is the most preponderant. Then if it is said: This results in preferring one who is not infallible over one who is infallible, the answer is: Infallibility has no bearing on preference; it is not considered in it. Rather, consideration is given to the greater reward for worship. So the commoners of humanity have more reward than the commoners of the angels because of the hardship incurred by the commoners of humanity in their worship, unlike the commoners of the angels, for obedience is their innate disposition, so they do not experience hardship in it. His saying: 'And some of each may excel some of its other' — 'some' (ba‘ḍ) is in the nominative as subject, and 'its other' (ba‘ḍahu) is in the accusative as an advanced object of 'may excel' (yafḍulu) which follows it, and the sentence is the predicate of the subject. That is: And some of each of the prophets and angels may excel some of its other. And 'may' (qad) is for certainty. So some prophets, like the Messengers of Strong Will, are superior to other prophets, and some angels, like their leaders, are superior to other angels. And the summary of what the poet indicated first and last, while following the preponderant way in preference, is that our master Muhammad is the best of creation absolutely, followed by our master Ibrahim, then our master Musa, then our master 'Isa, then our master Nuh; these are the Messengers of Strong Will as previously mentioned, then the rest...
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining two lines of the poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' concerning the comparison between angels and prophets. The author first clarifies a demonstrative pronoun, then presents the Maturidi detailed view on preference. The Maturidi school distinguishes between leaders of angels (ru'asā') and common angels, and similarly between prophets and common humans (awliyā'). Their hierarchy: Prophets are superior to angelic leaders; angelic leaders are superior to common pious humans (like Abu Bakr and 'Umar); common pious humans are superior to common angels (like the Throne-bearers and Cherubim). The text explains that the common humans referred to are the righteous, not the sinful, as angels are certainly superior to sinners. It then addresses an objection: this preference seems to favor non-infallible humans over infallible angels, but it answers that infallibility is not the criterion—rather, the amount of reward earned through worship matters. Common humans face hardship in worship, earning more reward than common angels who are naturally obedient without effort. The commentary then explains the second line of the poem, which states that within each group, some members may excel others (e.g., the best prophets are the Messengers of Strong Will; the best angels are their leaders). Finally, it summarizes the preponderant view: Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation, followed in order by Ibrahim, Musa, 'Isa, and Nuh, then the rest. The text cuts off mid-sentence at 'then the rest'.

Key Terms
عصمة ('iṣma)
ثواب (thawāb)
مشقة (mashaqqa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that infallibility is the primary determinant of superiority in the sight of God.
Correction: The passage explains that infallibility is not considered in preference; the amount of reward from worship is the criterion.

Checkpoint
According to the answer in the passage, why do common pious humans have more reward than common angels?
A) Because humans are infallible
B) Because humans perform more acts of worship
C) Because humans experience hardship in worship
D) Because angels do not worship

Key Takeaway
Infallibility does not determine superiority; the reward earned through worship with hardship is the decisive factor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you worship, do you seek ease or do you embrace the hardship that multiplies your reward? Name one act of worship you have avoided because it felt difficult. Will you commit to performing it this week precisely because of that hardship?
?
Do you ever compare yourself to others and assume that your outward piety (or lack of sin) makes you superior? How does this passage expose the false security of that thinking? Write down one instance where you have looked down on someone else's worship, and resolve to replace that with humility.
?
If reward is based on hardship, what does that say about your complaints regarding the difficulty of worship? Will you thank Allah for that difficulty instead? Make a specific intention to perform one hard act of worship this week for the very reason that it is hard.

intermediate

Within-Group Excellence and the Ranking of Prophets
Al-Laqqani explains intra-group excellence and gives a summary ranking of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that within each group (prophets and angels) some members excel others, and that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation.

Core Idea
Among prophets, the 'Messengers of Strong Will' are superior; among angels, leaders excel; Muhammad is the best of all.

After establishing the inter-group hierarchy, the poet adds a line about intra-group excellence. Al-Laqqani explains the grammar and meaning, then provides a summary ranking of the prophets from Muhammad down to the rest, affirming the supremacy of the Prophet Muhammad over all. This passage gives a complete picture of the Maturidi view on relative excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the grammatically explained line
Read the Arabic line and its translation. Notice the grammatical analysis: 'some' (ba‘ḍ) is subject, 'its other' (ba‘ḍahu) is object, 'may excel' (yafḍulu) is verb.
2
Understand intra-group excellence
The passage explains that some prophets (like Ul al-Azm) are superior to other prophets, and some angels (like their leaders) are superior to other angels.
3
Study the summary ranking
The commentary provides a list of the best prophets in order: Muhammad (best of all), then Ibrahim, Musa, Isa, Nuh, then the rest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception & Correction

Checkpoint
According to the summary in the passage, who is the best of all creation?
A) Prophet Ibrahim
B) Prophet Musa
C) Prophet Muhammad
D) Prophet Nuh

Key Takeaway
Some prophets and angels excel others within their category, and Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation, followed by the other Messengers of Strong Will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the best of all creation. But when you evaluate your own day, does your behavior reflect that he is the most important person in your life? If not, what will you do about it today?
?
The source teaches that some prophets are superior to others. Does your heart accept this ranking without envy or resentment towards any prophet? Are there any prophets you feel closer to that might cause you to subtly resist this hierarchy? If so, what does that reveal about your faith?

Unseen Matters
intermediate
6 min
Muhammad's Law is Not Abrogated
Defines naskh and asserts the non-abrogation of Muhammad's law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of naskh (abrogation) and why Prophet Muhammad's law is never replaced until the end of time.

Core Idea
Muhammad's law is final—no sharia comes after it until the world ends.

This lesson introduces a key teaching about Muhammad's prophethood: that his law is not subject to abrogation. The passage explains the meaning of 'abrogation' (naskh) and shows why the finality of prophethood implies the permanence of his sharia until time itself ends.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overall sense of the argument.
The passage combines a verse line with commentary.
2
Understand the conditional reasoning
Note that the non-abrogation is based on two premises: Muhammad is the seal of prophets, and his mission is universal. Identify the implied condition.
The 'fa' indicates a result of these premises.
3
Learn the definitions of naskh
The passage gives linguistic and technical definitions of naskh. Notice that the technical definition is 'lifting a legal ruling by a legal proof' and why the ruling itself cannot be lifted.
The ruling is Allah's eternal speech; only its temporal connection to people ends.
4
Interpret 'until time is abrogated'
Understand that 'naskh' of time means removal of time itself at the Day of Resurrection, not a replacement of Muhammad's law.
A hadith supports that the community remains upon truth until the Hour.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧٠ - بِعْتَتَهُ فَشَرْعُهُ لا يُنْسَخُ بِغَيرِهِ حَتَّى الزَّمانُ يُنْسَخُ) قوله : (لا يُنْسَخُ بِغَيرِهِ) هذا مفرّع على ختم النبوة به، وتعميم بعثته، فالفاء للتفريع، ويصح أن تكون فاء الفصيحة؛ لأنها أفصحت عن شرط مُقدر، والتقدير : إذا علمت أنه خاتم النبيين، وأن بعثته عامة فشرعه لا يُنسخ بغيره؛ لا كُلَّا ولا بعضاً. والشرع لغة البيان، واصطلاحاً الأحكام الشرعية . والنسخ لغةٌ : الإزالة والنقل، ومنه نسخت الشمس الظل؛ أي: أزالته، ونسخت الكتاب؛ أي نقلته وهل هو حقيقةٌ في المعنيين، أو حقيقة في الأول مجاز في الثاني، أو بالعكس؟ أقوال وخير الأمور أوساطها، فالصحيح أنه حقيقة في الأول مجاز في الثاني. واصطلاحاً : رفع حكم شرعي بدليل شرعي، والمراد برفع الحكم الشرعي انقطاع تعلقه بالمكلفين؛ لأنه خطاب الله تعالى، وهو يستحيل رفعه لأنه قديم، بخلاف التعلق فلا يستحيل رفعه لأنه حادث. وقوله : (حَتَّى الزَّمانُ يُنْسَخُ ) أي : فشرعه مستمر إلى نسخ الزمان، فالمراد بـ (حتى) الغاية مع كونها ابتدائية، و(الزمان) مبتدأ خبره (ينسخ)، والمراد بالنسخ هنا : المعنى اللغوي وهو الإزالة، فالمعنى: حتى الزمان يُزال ويرفع بحضور يوم القيامة لقوله : لا تزال هذه الأمةُ قائمة على أمر الله - يعني الدين الحق - لا يضرهم من خالفهم حتى يأتي أمر الله؛ أي: الساعة، وهو على حذف مضاف؛ أي: قربها ؛ لأن المؤمنين يموتون قبل الساعة بريح لينة، والمراد بالنسخ في آخر الشطر الأول: المعنى الشرعي؛ ففي كلامه الجناس، وقد تقدَّم الكلام في الإيطاء، فلا حاجة إلى الإعادة.
70: 'Because of his mission, his law is not abrogated by another, until time is abrogated.' His saying: 'not abrogated by another' is a result of the seal of prophethood upon him and the universality of his mission. The letter 'fa' is for result, and it can be the 'fa' of explicitness because it reveals an implied condition: if you know that he is the seal of the prophets and that his mission is universal, then his law is not abrogated by another, neither completely nor partially. 'Shar'' linguistically means clarification; technically, it means legal rulings. 'Naskh' linguistically means removal and transfer; from it is 'the sun abrogated the shade' i.e., removed it, and 'I abrogated the book' i.e., copied it. Is it literal in both meanings, or literal in the first and metaphorical in the second, or vice versa? There are sayings, and the best of matters is their middle: the correct view is that it is literal in the first and metaphorical in the second. Technically: lifting a legal ruling by a legal proof. By 'lifting the legal ruling' is meant the cessation of its connection to the obligated; because it is the speech of Allah, exalted, and its lifting is impossible because it is eternal, unlike the connection, which is not impossible to lift because it is temporal. His saying: 'until time is abrogated' means his law continues until the abrogation of time. 'Until' here indicates a terminus, while being inceptive; 'time' is the subject with 'is abrogated' as its predicate. The intended meaning of 'naskh' here is the linguistic sense: removal. So the meaning: until time is removed and raised at the arrival of the Day of Resurrection, because of his saying: 'This community will not cease to be established upon the command of Allah – meaning the true religion – unharmed by those who oppose them, until the command of Allah comes;' i.e., the Hour; and it involves an omitted genitive construction: i.e., its proximity, because the believers die before the Hour by a gentle wind. The intended meaning of 'naskh' at the end of the first hemistich is the technical sense; thus in his speech there is paronomasia (jinās), and discussion of it in the section on iṭā' has preceded, so there is no need to repeat.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage provides a definition and explanation of the ruling that Prophet Muhammad's law is not abrogated by any other. It begins with the verse line and explains that it is a result of the seal of prophethood and the universality of his mission. The definition of 'shar'' and 'naskh' is given both linguistically and technically. The discussion of whether naskh is literal in removal or transfer is settled: it is literal in removal and metaphorical in transfer. The technical definition is 'lifting a legal ruling by a legal proof', with the clarification that the ruling itself (as Allah's eternal speech) cannot be lifted; only the temporal connection to the obligated is lifted. Then it interprets 'until time is abrogated' as meaning the continuation of Muhammad's law until the end of time, where 'naskh' means removal. A hadith is cited to support that the community remains upon the truth until the Hour comes. Finally, it notes that the naskh in the first hemistich is technical, creating paronomasia with the earlier usage.

Key Terms
نسخ
شرع
ختم النبوة
رفع الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'naskh' of time means Muhammad's law might be replaced by another law before the end.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'naskh' of time means removal of time itself at the Day of Resurrection, not replacement of the law.

Checkpoint
What is the technical definition of naskh according to this passage?
A) Abrogation of a ruling by another
B) Lifting a legal ruling by a legal proof
C) Transfer of a ruling from one law to another
D) Removal of a legal text

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's sharia remains valid and unreplaced until the end of time, when the world itself is removed.

?

The Necessity of Abrogation by Muhammad's Law
Asserts that Muhammad's law abrogates all previous laws and refutes objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine that Muhammad's law abrogates all previous laws, the evidence for it, and the refutation of objections.

Core Idea
Muhammad's law abrogates all previous laws necessarily; benefits vary by time, not divine ignorance.

In this lesson, we explore a key doctrine about the finality of Muhammad's prophethood: his law abrogates all previous laws. The passage presents the evidence and answers objections from Jews and Christians. Let's delve into the source text.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse line and its explanation
Start by reading the Arabic verse line and its commentary. Notice how the commentator explains 'necessarily' as a condition of the occurrence.
2
Examine the evidence
The passage cites Quran 3:85, numerous hadith reaching tawatur, and consensus of Muslims. Consider why these three sources establish the doctrine.
3
Understand the objection and its refutation
Jews and Christians object that abrogation implies a benefit hidden from Allah. The refutation explains that benefits differ by time. Ponder how this answer preserves divine wisdom.
4
Note the supplication against deniers
The second hemistich is a prayer that Allah humiliates those who deny this abrogation. This underscores the seriousness of the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧١ - وَنَسْخُهُ لِشَرْعِ غَيْرِهِ وَقَعْ حَتْماً أَذَلَّ اللهُ مَنْ لَهُ مَنَعْ قوله : (وَنَسْخُهُ لِشَرْعِ غَيْرِهِ وَقَعْ حَتْماً) أي: ونسخ شرع نبينا محمد لشرع كل غيره، وقع وحصل حال كونه متحتماً، فـ (حتماً) بمعنى متحتماً حال من فاعل (وقع)، ويدل لذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا﴾ [آل عمران: ٨٥] الآية، والأحاديث في ذلك كثيرة بلغت جملتها مبلغ التواتر، فنسخ مشرعه الشرع غيره واقع سماعاً بإجماع المسلمين خلافاً لليهود والنصارى، حيث زعموا أن شرع نبينا لم ينسخ شرع أحدٍ من الأنبياء توسلاً للقول بنفي نبوته، واحتجوا على ذلك بأنه يلزم على القول بالنسخ ظهور مصلحةٍ كانت خفية على الله تعالى ورُدَّ بأن المصلحة تختلف الأزمنة، فالمصلحة في زمن الأمم السابقة اقتضت تكليفهم بشرائعهم، والمصلحة في زماننا اقتضت تكليفنا بشريعتنا وقوله : (أَذَلَّ اللهُ مَنْ لَهُ مَنَعْ) أي : ألحق الذلَّ بمن منع نسخ شرع نبينا لغيره، وهذه جملة دعائية على اليهود والنصارى فإنهم المانعون لذلك.
71: 'And his abrogation of the law of others occurred necessarily; Allah humiliates whoever denies it.' His saying: 'his abrogation of the law of others occurred necessarily' means: the abrogation of the law of our Prophet Muhammad for the law of everyone else occurred and took place as a necessity. So 'necessarily' means 'necessitated', as a condition of the subject of 'occurred'. This is indicated by the verse of Allah: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam...' (Quran 3:85) and the hadiths on that are many, reaching the level of tawatur. So the abrogation of the law of others by his law occurred by consensus of the Muslims, unlike the Jews and Christians, who claimed that the law of our Prophet did not abrogate the law of any of the prophets as a means to deny his prophethood. They argued that abrogation would imply the appearance of a benefit that was hidden from Allah, but it was replied that benefits differ according to times: the benefit in the time of previous nations necessitated obligating them with their laws, and the benefit in our time necessitated obligating us with our law. His saying: 'Allah humiliates whoever denies it' means: He inflicts humiliation on whoever denies the abrogation of our Prophet's law for others, and this is an imprecatory sentence against the Jews and Christians, for they are the ones who deny it.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage asserts that Prophet Muhammad's law abrogates all previous laws necessarily. It begins with the verse line, explaining that 'necessarily' indicates the occurrence is a certain fact. Evidence from the Quran (3:85) and numerous hadith reaching the level of tawatur is cited. The consensus of Muslims is that this abrogation is a known fact, contrary to Jews and Christians who deny it. Their objection is that abrogation would imply that a benefit was hidden from Allah. The response refutes this by noting that benefits differ according to times – past nations benefited from their laws, while we benefit from ours. The second hemistich is a supplication that Allah humiliates those who deny this abrogation, specifically directed at the Jews and Christians who oppose it.

Misconception: Abrogation implies that Allah was unaware of what was beneficial until later.
Correction: Benefits vary with time; Allah's wisdom decreed different laws for different eras, not a change in His knowledge.

Key Takeaway

Abrogation in Islamic Law: Permissible and Occurred
Declares permissibility and occurrence of abrogation, refutes rational ethics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that abrogation of some parts of Islamic law by others is both permissible and has actually occurred, and that the basis for good and evil is divine law rather than independent reason.

Core Idea
Good and evil are defined by divine law, not reason; abrogation can apply to any ruling.

This passage from Sanusi's 'Umm al-Barahin' tackles the question of abrogation within the Sharia of Prophet Muhammad. It affirms that abrogation is allowed and has happened, and then responds to those who argue that certain essential obligations cannot be abrogated because they are rationally good or evil. The key point is that good and evil are determined by revelation, not reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read both versions to grasp the complete argument. Notice the poetic line and the commentary that follows.
The passage combines a theological verse with a detailed refutation.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Look for the rationalist position (knowledge is rationally good, disbelief rationally evil) and the Ash'ari response (good and evil are determined by divine law).
This is the core doctrinal debate in the passage.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the Ash'ari position allows for abrogation of any ruling, including obligations like knowing Allah. How does this shape Islamic theology?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧٢ - وَنَسْخَ بَعْضِ شَرْعِهِ بِالْبَعْضِ أَجِزُ وما فِي ذَا لَهُ مِنْ غَضٌ قوله : (وَنَسْخَ بَعْضِ شَرْعِهِ بِالبَعْضِ أَجِزْ ) لا يخفى أن (نسخ) بالنصب مفعول مقدَّمٌ لـ ( أجز) الواقع بعده؛ أي: اعتقد جواز نسخ بعض شرعه بالبعض الآخر جوازاً وقوعيّا؛ لأن ذلك وقع بالفعل نعم وجوب معرفته تعالى وتحريم الكفر نسخه غير واقع، وإن كان جائزاً كما هو مذهب أهل الحق خلافاً لمن قال : (إن المعرفة حَسَنٌ عقلي، والكفر قبيح عقلي، فوجوب المعرفة وتحريم الكفر لا يجوز نسخهما)، ونحن نقول : الحسن ما حسَّنه الشرع والقبيح ما قبَّحه الشرع، فلو جعل المعرفة من القبيح، والكفر من الحسن فلا حرج عليه . وشمل البعض المنسوخ البعض القرآني خلافاً لمن منعه كأبي [مسلم].
72: 'And allow abrogation of part of his law by another part; there is no objection in this for him.' His saying: 'allow abrogation of part of his law by another part' – it is not hidden that 'abrogation' (naskha) is in the accusative as a preposed object of 'allow' (ajiz) that comes after it; meaning: believe in the permissibility of abrogation of some of his law by another part with actual permissibility, because that actually occurred. Yes, the obligation of knowing Him and the prohibition of disbelief – their abrogation has not occurred, although it is permissible, as is the doctrine of the people of truth, contrary to those who said: 'Knowledge of Allah is rationally good, and disbelief is rationally evil, so the obligation of knowledge and prohibition of disbelief cannot be abrogated.' We say: Good is what the law makes good, and evil is what the law makes evil. So if He were to make knowledge evil and disbelief good, there would be no objection. And the abrogated part includes the Quranic part, contrary to those who prohibit it, like Abu Muslim.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility and occurrence of abrogation within the Sharia of Prophet Muhammad. The verse line commands the reader to believe in the permissibility of abrogating some parts of the law by others, and that such abrogation actually occurred. It then clarifies that certain essential obligations (like knowing Allah) and prohibitions (like disbelief) have not been abrogated, though they are theoretically abrogable. This is the position of Ahl al-Haqq, as opposed to those who claim that good and evil are rational categories, thus making such obligations and prohibitions immutable. The response is that good and evil are determined by divine law, not by reason; if Allah prescribed otherwise, it would be valid. Finally, the passage notes that abrogation can affect Quranic verses, contrary to the view of Abu Muslim al-Isfahani who denied that.

Key Terms
نسخ
جواز وقوعي
حسن وقبح عقلي
القرآني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Good and evil are independent rational categories, so obligations like knowing Allah cannot be abrogated.
Correction: Good and evil are determined by divine law; Allah could make something good or evil if He willed, so any ruling is theoretically abrogable.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for good and evil?
A) Rational judgment
B) Divine law (shar‘)
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Prophetic tradition

Key Takeaway
Abrogation within Islamic law is permissible and has occurred; good and evil are defined by revelation, not reason.

Abrogation: Two Stations – Permissibility and Occurrence
Author summarizes the debate on abrogation into two stations: permissibility and occurrence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the permissibility of abrogation (jawaz) and its actual occurrence (wuqu') in Islamic theology, and how this distinction resolves concerns about deficiency in the Quran.

Core Idea
Abrogation is possible in theory but not all of it has actually occurred.

The debate on abrogation often confuses two separate questions: Can abrogation happen at all? And has it happened in every case? This passage from the commentary clarifies these two levels—known as jawaz and wuqu'—and addresses an objection about the integrity of the Quran by distinguishing abrogation of the whole from abrogation of parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection from Al-Isfahani
Read how Al-Isfahani uses Quran 41:42 to argue that if any part of the Quran were abrogated, falsehood would enter it. This sets up the need for a careful distinction.
The verse says falsehood cannot approach the Quran from any direction.
2
Understand the response by earlier scholars
Note how they explain that the pronoun in the verse refers to the whole Quran, which is not abrogated by consensus. The author's restriction to 'some' (ba'd) excludes abrogation of the entire Quran.
Abrogation of the whole is theoretically possible but has not occurred.
3
Grasp the two-station distinction
The passage explicitly divides the discussion into two stations: permissibility (jawaz) and occurrence (wuqu'). In permissibility, abrogation of the entire Shari'a or part of it is allowed. In occurrence, abrogation of the whole has not happened.
4
Apply the distinction to the poet's line
The line 'And there is no deficiency in this for him' means allowing partial abrogation does not imply any deficiency that would make abrogation impossible.
This reinforces that abrogation is not a flaw in divine revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصفهاني مُحتجا بقوله تعالى: لَا يَأْتِيهِ الْبَاطِلُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَلَا مِنْ خَلْفِهِ (فصلت: ٤٢) فلو نسخ بعضه لتطرق إليه البطلان . وأجاب الأولون بأن الضمير لمجموع القرآن وهو لا ينسخ اتفاقاً، وخرج بتقييد المصنف بالبعض نسخ الجميع، فهو وإن كان جائزاً لكنه غير واقع. فالحاصل أن الكلام في مقامين : مقام جواز ومقام وقوع، فمن حيث الجواز يجوز نسخ الشريعة كلا أو بعضاً، وأما من حيث الوقوع فلا يجوز نسخ الجميع جوازاً وقوعيا. وقوله : (وما فِي ذَا لَهُ مِنْ غَضَ) أي : وما في هذا الحكم، وهو تجويز نسخ بعض شرعه بالبعض الآخر من نقص يقتضي امتناعه.
Al-Isfahani argued with His statement, the Exalted: 'Falsehood cannot approach it from before or behind it' (Fussilat: 42). So if some of it were abrogated, falsehood would have access to it. And the earlier scholars answered that the pronoun refers to the entirety of the Qur'an, which is not abrogated by agreement, and the author restricted [the discussion] by [the word] 'some' to the abrogation of the whole, which, although permissible, has not occurred. So the conclusion is that the discussion is in two stations: the station of permissibility and the station of occurrence. In terms of permissibility, it is permissible to abrogate the law entirely or partially, but in terms of occurrence, it is not permissible to abrogate the whole as a matter of actual occurrence. And his statement: 'And there is no deficiency in this for him' means: And there is no deficiency in this ruling, which is permitting the abrogation of some of His law by other parts of it, that would necessitate its impossibility.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and a classification. It begins with an objection from al-Isfahani, who argued that if any part of the Qur'an were abrogated, falsehood would enter it, citing Quran 41:42. The earlier scholars respond that the pronoun in the verse refers to the whole Qur'an, which remains unabrogated by consensus. They note that the author's mention of 'some' (some of the Shari'a) excludes abrogation of the entire Qur'an, which, though theoretically possible, has not occurred. The author then summarizes the debate by distinguishing between two levels: the level of permissibility (jawaz) and the level of actual occurrence (wuqu'). In terms of permissibility, abrogation of the entire Shari'a or part of it is allowed; in terms of occurrence, abrogation of the entire Shari'a has not happened. Finally, the author explains the poet's line 'And there is no deficiency in this for him' to mean that allowing abrogation of some parts by others does not imply any deficiency that would make it impossible.

Key Terms
نسخ
جواز
وقوع
ضمير
البطلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that abrogation implies deficiency in the Qur'an.
Correction: The author clarifies that abrogation only applies to specific parts and does not affect the whole, so no deficiency is implied.

Checkpoint
What is the two-station distinction regarding naskh according to the passage?
A) Permissibility and necessity
B) Permissibility and actual occurrence
C) Abrogation of the whole and the part
D) Abrogation of the Qur'an and the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Abrogation is theoretically possible for the entire Shari'a but has only occurred partially, and this does not imply any deficiency in the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that abrogation of some rulings is permitted and has occurred. When you encounter an abrogated ruling from the past, do you fully trust that it was perfectly wise for its time, or does a part of you question why it was changed? How can you increase your trust in the All-Wise?
?
Al-Isfahani's argument suggests that any abrogation might imply deficiency. Have you ever secretly thought that a particular Islamic ruling was outdated or incomplete? How does this lesson's distinction between permissibility and occurrence challenge your assumptions?
?
The response emphasizes that the whole Qur'an is preserved from falsehood. Do you ever entertain doubts about the authenticity of the divine message? How does the certainty that 'falsehood cannot approach it' strengthen your conviction in every letter of the Qur'an?

Four Types of Abrogation Between Quran and Sunnah
Enumerates four types of abrogation with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four types of abrogation involving the Quran and Sunnah, with examples from revealed texts.

Core Idea
Later revelation abrogates earlier, whether Quran or Sunnah.

The author now turns to the mechanics of abrogation, specifically how later rulings override earlier ones between the Quran and Sunnah. He enumerates four combinations and supports each with a clear example from revelation. This lesson will help you trace how Islamic law develops through abrogation across different sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four types
Carefully read the Arabic passage and note the four combinations: Book by Book, Sunnah by Sunnah, Sunnah by Book, and Book by Sunnah.
Each type is introduced with 'نسخ' and a conjunction.
2
Examine the examples for each type
For each type, the author provides a specific example from the Quran or hadith. Understand how the later source abrogates the earlier one.
Notice the principle: later in time, even if the earlier text appears first in recitation.
3
Understand the principle of tard (later) abrogating qadim (earlier)
The key criterion is chronological order, not the status of the source. A later hadith can abrogate an earlier Quranic verse, and vice versa.
This is based on the consensus of Sunni scholars.
4
Reflect on the significance for Islamic law
Abrogation shows that Islamic law was revealed progressively, with later rulings superseding earlier ones. This ensures the final ruling is applicable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل ما ذكر نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةً لِأَزْوَاجِهِم مَّتَاعًا إِلَى الْحَوْلِ غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٍ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤٠] فإنه نُسخ بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] لتأخره نزولاً، وإن تقدَّم تلاوة. ونسخ السنة بالسنة كما في حديث: كنت نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور فزوروها، فإنه نسخ النهي الذي وقع منه أولاً بالأمر في هذا الحديث. ونسخ السنة بالكتاب كما في استقبال بيت المقدس الثابت بالسنة، فإنه نسخ باستقبال الكعبة الثابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَوَلِّ وَجْهَكَ شَطْرَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٤٤]. ونسخ الكتاب بالسنة كما في قوله تعالى : كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالأَقْرَبِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٠] ، فإنه نسخ بحديث: «لا وصية لوارث».
And included in what was mentioned is abrogation of the Book by the Book, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'And those who are taken from among you and leave wives, a bequest for their wives: maintenance for one year without eviction' (al-Baqara 2:240), for it was abrogated by His statement, the Exalted: 'And those who are taken from among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days' (al-Baqara 2:234) because it was later in revelation, even though it is recited earlier. And abrogation of the Sunnah by the Sunnah, as in the hadith: 'I had forbidden you from visiting graves, so visit them,' for it abrogates the prohibition that first came from him by the command in this hadith. And abrogation of the Sunnah by the Book, as in facing the direction of Jerusalem established by the Sunnah, for it was abrogated by facing the Kaaba established by His statement, the Exalted: 'So turn your face toward al-Masjid al-Haram' (al-Baqara 2:144). And abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, a bequest for parents and relatives' (al-Baqara 2:180), for it was abrogated by the hadith: 'No bequest to an heir.'
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of four types of abrogation supported by examples from the Quran and Sunnah. The author lists: (1) Abrogation of the Quran by the Quran, exemplified by the verse on bequest for widows (2:240) abrogated by the waiting period verse (2:234). (2) Abrogation of the Sunnah by the Sunnah, as in the Prophet's initial prohibition of visiting graves later abrogated by his permission. (3) Abrogation of the Sunnah by the Quran, as in the direction of prayer changed from Jerusalem to the Kaaba by Quranic revelation (2:144). (4) Abrogation of the Quran by the Sunnah, as in the inheritance verse (2:180) abrogated by the hadith prohibiting bequests to heirs. The principle is that the later revealed source abrogates the earlier, regardless of the source type.

Key Terms
نسخ
كتاب
سنة
تلاوة
نزول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sunnah cannot abrogate the Quran.
Correction: The author provides a clear example: the verse on bequests to parents and relatives (2:180) was abrogated by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir.' Thus, the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran when it is later in time.

Checkpoint
Which type of abrogation is exemplified by the change of prayer direction from Jerusalem to the Kaaba?
A) Book by Book
B) Sunnah by Sunnah
C) Sunnah by Book
D) Book by Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Abrogation can occur between the Quran and Sunnah in all four combinations, with the later revelation taking precedence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet initially forbade visiting graves, then permitted it. Is there an area of your life where you cling to an old practice or understanding, even though clear evidence from revelation has come to supersede it? What would it take for you to truly submit and change?
?
The abrogating verse on the widow's waiting period was revealed later, even though it appears earlier in the Quran. When you read the Quran, do you seek to understand the chronological context, or do you take it at face value? What might you be missing by ignoring this?
?
The Quranic command to bequeath to parents was abrogated by a hadith. Do you fully accept that the Prophet's words carry the same weight as the Quran in terms of legislative authority? Or is there a part of you that hesitates to follow a ruling that comes from Sunnah alone? Examine your heart.

Types of Abrogation: Recitation and Ruling
Author classifies naskh into types involving recitation and ruling, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of naskh based on their effect on recitation and ruling, and be able to identify examples for each.

Core Idea
Naskh can affect recitation, ruling, or both — each has distinct examples.

In this passage, Sanusi explains how abrogation can apply differently to the text of a verse and its legal ruling. He presents three categories: abrogation of both recitation and ruling, abrogation of recitation only (like the stoning verse), and abrogation of ruling only (like the bequest verse). Understanding these distinctions helps clarify the complex relationship between Quranic text and Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice the author's classification of three types.
Pay attention to the examples: sucklings, stoning, bequest.
2
Identify the three categories
From the passage, extract the three categories: (1) abrogation of both recitation and ruling, (2) abrogation of recitation only, (3) abrogation of ruling only.
3
Analyze the examples
For each category, note the specific example given and how it fits the definition. Understand why the stoning verse example is important.
4
Reflect on the disagreement
Notice the difference between 'our view' and the Malikis regarding the sucklings example. This shows there can be scholarly differences on what was abrogated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل أيضاً نسخ التلاوة والحكم جميعاً، كما في نحو (عشر رضعات معلومات يُحرمن) فإنه كان مما يُتلى ، فنُسخ بـ(خمس معلومات يحرمن)، ثم نسخ هذا الناسخ عندنا تلاوةً لا حُكماً، وعند المالكية تلاوةً وحُكماً، ونسخ التلاوة دون الحكم كما في نحو الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما ألبنَّة نكالاً مِنَ الله والله عزيز حكيم، فإنه كان مما يُتلى فنسخ تلاوة لا حكماً، ونسخ الحكم دون التلاوة كما في آية: ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا وَصِيَّةُ لِأَزْوَاجِهِم مَّتَاعًا إِلَى الْحَوْلِ غَيْرَ إِخْرَاجٍ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٢٤٠] فإنه نُسخ حكماً بآية أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٢٣٤] ويبقى تلاوة.
And it also includes abrogation of both recitation and ruling together, as in (ten known sucklings make unlawful), for it was something recited, then it was abrogated by (five known sucklings make unlawful), then this abrogator was abrogated in our view in recitation only, not in ruling, while according to the Malikis in both recitation and ruling. And abrogation of recitation without ruling, as in (the old man and old woman, if they commit fornication, stone them both as a punishment from Allah, and Allah is Mighty, Wise), for it was something recited, then its recitation was abrogated but not its ruling. And abrogation of ruling without recitation, as in the verse: 'And those who are taken from among you and leave wives, a bequest for their wives: maintenance for one year without eviction' (al-Baqara 2:240), for it was abrogated in ruling by the verse of 'four months and ten' (al-Baqara 2:234), while its recitation remains.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a classification of abrogation by its effect on recitation (tilaawa) and ruling (hukm). The author lists three subtypes: (1) Abrogation of both recitation and ruling, as in the verse about ten known sucklings being abrogated by five known sucklings, and then the abrogating verse itself had its recitation abrogated while the ruling remained (according to the author's school), whereas the Malikis hold both were abrogated. (2) Abrogation of recitation only, as in the stoning verse for adulterers whose text is no longer recited but the ruling is still applied. (3) Abrogation of ruling only, as in the bequest verse (2:240) where the ruling (maintenance for a year) is abrogated by the waiting period verse (2:234), but the text remains in the Quran.

الرجم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if a verse is abrogated in recitation, its ruling is also abrogated.
Correction: The stoning verse example shows ruling can remain even after recitation is abrogated.

Checkpoint
What type of abrogation is exemplified by the stoning verse whose recitation is abrogated but the ruling remains?
A) Abrogation of ruling only
B) Abrogation of recitation only
C) Abrogation of both
D) Abrogation of neither

Key Takeaway
The same verse can be abrogated in different ways: its text, its ruling, or both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Abrogation Always Has a Replacement (Badal)
Argument for necessary replacement in abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that abrogation in Islamic law always involves a replacement (badal) according to al-Shafi'i, and how the objection regarding the charity-for-consultation verse is addressed.

Core Idea
Abrogation always leaves a replacement behind — even when it seems to vanish.

This lesson examines a key principle of Islamic jurisprudence regarding abrogation (naskh). The author sides with Imam al-Shafi'i in asserting that every abrogated ruling is replaced by another ruling, whether of equal, lighter, or heavier weight. The passage addresses the objection that some abrogations appear to have no replacement, using the example of the obligation to give charity before private consultation with the Prophet (58:12). This lesson will guide you through the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the verse references.
2
Identify the two opposing views
The passage contrasts the view of al-Shafi'i (always with replacement) with the view of those who say sometimes without replacement. Find the sentence that articulates each view.
The opposing view is introduced with 'خلافاً لمن قال'.
3
Examine the examples
The passage gives two examples: the al-Anfal verses (with replacement) and the al-Mujadila verse (seemingly without). Notice how the author uses these examples to illustrate the debate.
The al-Anfal verses show a lighter obligation replacing a heavier one.
4
Understand the author's resolution
The author resolves the apparent counterexample by arguing that even the charity-for-consultation verse has a replacement: the permissibility or recommendation of charity. See how this counters the opposing view.
This shows that the replacement is not always an obligation.
5
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider why the principle that abrogation must have a replacement is important for understanding the continuity of divine legislation.
This principle ensures that no ruling is lifted without providing guidance in its place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحق أن النسخ لا يكون إلا إلى بدل كما قاله الإمام الشافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه خلافاً لمن قال: تارة يكون إلى بدل كما في آيتي الأنفال؛ أعني قوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ حَرِّضِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عَلَى الْقِتَالِ إِن يَكُن مِّنكُمْ عِشْرُونَ صَبِرُونَ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْنِ [الأنفال : ٦٥] الآية، وقوله تعالى: الْآنَ خَفَّفَ اللهُ عَنكُمْ وَعَلِمَ أَنَّ فِيكُمْ ضَعْفًا فَإِن يَكُن مِّنكُم مِائَةٌ صَابِرَةٌ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْنِ [الأنفال : ٦٦] الآية، وتارة يكون إلى غير بدل كما في قوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا نَاجَيْتُمُ الرَّسُولَ [المجادلة : ١٢] الآية، فإن وجوب الصدقة على مناجاة الرسول نسخ بلا بدل، وعلى الأول فبدل هذا الوجوب جواز التصدق أو استحبابه، فلم يقع بلا بدل أصلاً.
And the truth is that abrogation only occurs with a replacement, as al-Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, said, contrary to those who say: sometimes it is with a replacement, as in the two verses of al-Anfal, namely His statement, the Exalted: 'O Prophet, urge the believers to fight. If there are twenty steadfast among you, they will overcome two hundred' (al-Anfal 8:65) and His statement, the Exalted: 'Now Allah has lightened [the burden] from you and knows that among you is weakness. So if there are a hundred steadfast among you, they will overcome two hundred' (al-Anfal 8:66), and sometimes it is without a replacement, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, when you [wish to] privately consult the Messenger...' (al-Mujadila 58:12), for the obligation of charity before private consultation was abrogated without a replacement. According to the first view, the replacement of this obligation is the permissibility or recommendation of charity, so it never occurred without a replacement at all.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the position that abrogation always entails a replacement (badal). The author sides with al-Shafi'i against those who claim some abrogations occur without a replacement. The opponents cite the two verses of al-Anfal (8:65-66) as an example of abrogation with a replacement (the earlier command to fight was replaced by a lighter duty). They also cite the verse of private consultation with the Prophet (58:12) as an example of abrogation without a replacement, since the obligation of giving charity before consultation was lifted entirely. The author counters by adopting the first view: even in that case, the replacement is the permissibility or recommendation of giving charity, so there is always some replacement. Thus, no abrogation occurs without a substitute.

Key Terms
بدل
نسخ
الأنفال
المجادلة
الصدقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation can remove a ruling completely without providing a substitute.
Correction: According to al-Shafi'i and this author, every abrogation has a replacement, even if it is merely a permissibility or recommendation, as in the case of the charity obligation before consultation.

Checkpoint
According to the author and al-Shafi'i, what is the replacement for the abrogated obligation of charity before private consultation with the Prophet?
A) No replacement
B) Permissibility or recommendation of charity
C) An alternative act of worship
D) A different charity amount

Key Takeaway
Every abrogation in Islamic law is accompanied by a replacement ruling, ensuring continuity of divine legislation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When Allah replaces a ruling in your life—whether through changing circumstances or new understanding—do you see it as a sign of His mercy and wisdom, or do you resist the change because you miss the old duty? This lesson teaches that every abrogation has a replacement. Are you actively looking for the wisdom and new path He has provided, or are you stuck mourning what was removed? Commit today to trust His perfect replacement.
?
The verse about private consultation had a hidden replacement: the duty became permissible, not lost. Think of a time you felt Allah removed something dear or difficult from your life. Can you now see that He replaced it with something else—perhaps a lighter burden or a new opportunity for good? Will you thank Him for that replacement, even if it looks different from what you expected?

The Obligation to Believe in Aisha's Innocence
Commentary on the line affirming Aisha's innocence and ruling of kufr for deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in the innocence of Aisha (radiAllahu anha) from the slander and why denying or doubting it constitutes kufr.

Core Idea
Denying Aisha's innocence is not a minor error—it is kufr.

This passage from the commentary addresses a critical point of faith regarding the Mother of the Believers, Aisha. It establishes that her innocence from the slander is a matter of obligatory belief, supported by the Qur'an, consensus, and authentic hadith. The commentator then delivers the decisive ruling: anyone who denies or even doubts this commits disbelief (kufr). Let's examine the proofs and the ruling carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage is a commentary on a poetic line; the line itself is quoted at the beginning.
2
Identify the obligation
Find where the commentator states that believing in Aisha's innocence is obligatory (وجوباً). Understand that this is not optional but required in faith.
3
List the three proofs
The commentator cites three proofs: the Qur'an, the consensus of the ummah, and authentic hadith. Locate each one in the passage.
These proofs make the belief definitive.
4
Understand the ruling
Read the final sentence: 'فمن جحد براءتها أو شك فيها كفر'. Note that both denial and doubt are included, and the consequence is kufr.
This shows the severity of the matter.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this is a matter of kufr. It involves rejecting clear texts and consensus, and it attacks the honor of the Prophet's family.
This protects the integrity of revelation and the Prophet's household.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَبَرِّتَنْ لِعَائِشَهُ مِمَّا رَمَوا) بزيادة اللام وسكون الهاء للوزن؛ أي: اعتقد وجوباً براءة أم المؤمنين عائشة بنت أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنها وعن أبويها ممَّا رماها به المنافقون من الإفك ؛ أي: أشدّ الكذب والذي تولى كبره ؛ أي: معظمه حيث ابتدأ الخوض فيه، وأشاعه عبد الله بن أبي بن سلول لعنه الله، وأبي : اسم أبيه، وسَلُول : اسم أمه، وقد جاء القرآن ببراءتها، وانعقد عليها إجماع الأمة، ووردت بها الأحاديث الصحيحة، فمن جحد براءتها أو شك فيها كفر .
His statement: (and she was declared innocent of what they accused her) with an extra lam and sukun on the ha for meter; meaning: believe as an obligation the innocence of the Mother of the Believers Aisha bint Abi Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with her and her parents, from what the hypocrites accused her of from the slander; that is, the most severe lie, and the one who undertook its great part, i.e., its majority, where he began delving into it and spread it, Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul, may Allah curse him, and Ubayy is the name of his father, and Salul is the name of his mother. And the Quran has come with her innocence, and the consensus of the ummah is established upon it, and authentic hadiths have been reported concerning it. So whoever denies her innocence or doubts it, he disbelieves.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a poetic line from the poem. The commentator explains the line's meaning: it mandates obligatory belief in the absolute innocence of Aisha (radiAllahu anha) from the slander (ifk) fabricated by the hypocrites, led by Abdullah ibn Ubayy. The commentator then provides the proofs: the Quran (Surat an-Nur), consensus of the ummah, and authentic hadiths. Finally, he states the ruling: anyone who denies or even doubts her innocence commits kufr (disbelief).

Key Terms
براءة
الإفك
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Doubting or denying Aisha's innocence is a minor sin or excusable.
Correction: The text explicitly states that whoever denies or doubts her innocence commits kufr (disbelief).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on someone who doubts the innocence of Aisha (radiAllahu anha)?
A) He is a fasiq.
B) He is a kafir.
C) He is excused due to ignorance.
D) It depends on his intention.

Key Takeaway
The innocence of Aisha is a matter of consensus and revealed text; denial or doubt is kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that doubting Aisha's innocence is kufr, does your heart tremble with certainty, or is there a hidden hesitation you have never examined? What will you do today to remove any lingering doubt?
?
If you were in a gathering where someone subtly casts doubt on the character of the Mothers of the Believers, would you speak up with the truth of the Quran and consensus, or would you remain silent to avoid discomfort? What does your answer reveal about the strength of your iman?
?
The passage says denial or doubt is kufr. Have you ever allowed your own intellect or cultural narratives to create even a speck of doubt about what Allah and His Messenger have declared? What is the repentance for that?

Angelic Hosts and Iblis's Deception at Badr
Narrates the angelic appearance, Iblis's deception, and Prophet's sightings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the supernatural events at the Battle of Badr, including the appearance of angels, the role of Iblis, and the Prophet's encounters with Mika'il and Jibril.

Core Idea
Badr was a cosmic confrontation where angels fought and Iblis fled.

This passage from al-Sanusi describes the unseen dimensions of the Battle of Badr. Angels appeared in vast numbers, Iblis disguised himself to encourage the polytheists but fled when the angels arrived, and the Prophet himself witnessed Mika'il and Jibril. These events affirm that Allah supports His messengers with visible and invisible aid.

Guided Path
1
Read the angelic description
Notice the details of the angels' appearance: five thousand white men on piebald horses, with various turban colors, and the marks on the slain.
The description emphasizes both the grandeur and the variety of the angels.
2
Observe Iblis's role
Iblis takes the form of Suraqa ibn Malik, promises protection, but retreats when he sees Jibril.
His flight and prayer for respite show his powerlessness before divine command.
3
Reflect on the Prophet's smile
The Prophet smiles during prayer upon seeing Mika'il returning from pursuit, and later Jibril assures him of Allah's pleasure.
This shows the intimate connection between the Prophet and the angels.
4
Consider the significance
These events demonstrate that Badr was not merely a physical battle but a divinely orchestrated event with supernatural witnesses.

النبوات
بعضهم
بعضاً، ثم كملت خمسة آلاف فتمثلوا برجال بيض على خيل بُلْقٍ (۱) ، عمائمهم بيضُ قد أرخوا أطرافها بين أكتافهم وقيل : سُود، وقيل: صُفْر، وقيل: ، حُمْر ، وقيل خُضْر، فكأنهم أنواع وكان قتيلهم يُعرف بأثر السواد في الأعناق والبنان؛ أي: المفصل، مثل حَرْقِ النار (٢).
(۲)
وكان إبليس مع المشركين مُتصوّراً بصورة سراقة بن مالك، وكان معه راية، وقال : لا غالب لكم اليوم من الناس، وإني جارٌ لكم ؛ أي معين لكم فلما أقبل جبريل والملائكة نَكَصَ على عقبيه وقال : إني بريء منكم إني أرى ما لا ترون وصار يقول : اللهم إني أنشدك أني من المنظرين
·
(۳)
وتبسَّمَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في صلاته، فسألوه عن ذلك بعد انقضائها، فقال: «مَرَّ ميكائيل وعلى جناحيه أثر الغبارِ ، وهو راجع من طلب القوم، فضحكَ إِليَّ فتبسمْتُ بي إليه (4)، وجاءه جبريل بعد القتال على فرس أحمر عليه درعه ومعه رمحه، فقال: یا محمد ؛ إن الله بعثني إليك وأمرني ألا أفارقك حتى ترضى، هل رضيت؟ قال: نعم. والحكمة في قتال الملائكة وحضورهم مع المسلمين مع أن الملك الواحد كجبريل يقدر على رفع الكفار، بل على اقتلاع الأرض أن تكون الملائكة عدداً و مدداً لجيش المسلمين على عادة مدد الجيوش؛ رعاية لصورة الأسباب التي أجراها الله بين عباده.
قال ابن عباس (٥) : (ولم تقاتل الملائكة إلا يوم بدر، ولكنها تحضر في كل قتال من قتال الكفار إلى يوم القيامة لتكثير سواد المسلمين).
The prophecies [section]. Some of them [the angels] appeared to others, then they completed five thousand and appeared as white men on piebald horses (1), their turbans white, having let down their ends between their shoulders. And it was said: black, and it was said: yellow, and it was said: red, and it was said: green, so they were as if [different] kinds. And their slain was known by the trace of blackness on the necks and the fingertips; i.e., the joint, like the burning of fire (2). (2) And Iblis was with the polytheists, having taken the form of Suraqa ibn Malik, and with him was a banner, and he said: 'There is no victor over you today from the people, and I am a protector for you'; i.e., a helper for you. When Jibril and the angels approached, he retreated on his heels and said: 'I am innocent of you, I see what you do not see,' and he began to say: 'O Allah, I implore You [to grant] that I be among those who are given respite.' (3) And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, smiled during his prayer. They asked him about that after its completion, and he said: 'Mika'il passed by, and on his wings was the trail of dust, while he was returning from pursuing the people. He smiled at me, so I smiled back at him' (4). And Jibril came to him after the fighting on a red horse, wearing his armor and carrying his spear, and said: 'O Muhammad, Allah has sent me to you and commanded me not to leave you until you are pleased. Are you pleased?' He said: 'Yes.' And the wisdom in the angels' fighting and their presence with the Muslims, despite the fact that a single angel like Jibril is able to remove the disbelievers—indeed to uproot the earth—is that the angels are a number and a reinforcement for the army of the Muslims, following the custom of reinforcing armies; out of observance for the form of causes that Allah has established among His servants. Ibn Abbas (5) said: 'The angels did not fight except on the day of Badr, but they attend every battle against the disbelievers until the Day of Resurrection to increase the numbers of the Muslims.'
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the angels' participation in the Battle of Badr. It begins by describing the appearance of angels as five thousand white men on piebald horses with various turban colors. Their slain enemies could be identified by black marks on necks and fingers. Then it narrates Iblis's role: he appeared as Suraqa ibn Malik, encouraged the polytheists, but fled when he saw the angels, recanting his promise. The Prophet smiled during prayer, explaining that he saw Mika'il returning from pursuit. Jibril later came to assure the Prophet of Allah's pleasure. The author then explains the wisdom: although an individual angel like Jibril could annihilate the enemy single-handedly, Allah sent many angels as a reinforcement army to uphold the divine custom of secondary causes and to strengthen the Muslims. Ibn Abbas adds that angels only actually fought at Badr, but they attend all later battles to boost Muslim morale by their presence.

Key Terms
إبليس
جبريل
ميكائيل
بدر
سراقة بن مالك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the Prophet smile during prayer?
A) He saw Jibril coming with a spear
B) He saw Mika'il smiling at him after returning from pursuit
C) He heard good news about the battle
D) He saw the angels descending

Key Takeaway
The Battle of Badr was a manifestation of divine support, with angels visibly fighting and Iblis fleeing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult situation, do you look for the angels around you, or do you depend on worldly allies like the polytheists did? How can you train your heart to see the unseen support that Allah provides?
?
Iblis promised victory but fled when the angels came. In what areas of your life have you trusted in something or someone that ultimately abandoned you? Will you now turn fully to Allah, who never abandons His sincere servants?
?
The Prophet smiled at the sight of Mika'il returning from pursuit. Does the reality of divine help bring you genuine joy in the midst of your struggles, or have you become desensitized to the signs of Allah's care? What will you change to cultivate that joy?

intermediate
4 min
The Wisdom of Angelic Participation in Battle
Explains the wisdom of many angels and Ibn Abbas' ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reason why Allah sent many angels to fight at Badr, and the ongoing role of angels in battles according to Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Allah sent many angels to uphold the custom of secondary causes, not because He needed help.

After narrating the events of Badr, al-Sanusi addresses a potential question: if a single angel like Jibril could annihilate the enemy, why did Allah send thousands? The answer reveals a profound principle: Allah maintains the order of causes and effects to preserve the natural order. Ibn Abbas adds that angels only fought at Badr but attend all later battles to strengthen the Muslims spiritually.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
The passage asks: why were many angels sent when a single one could have destroyed the enemy?
This question arises from reflection on divine omnipotence.
2
Understand the answer
The wisdom is that angels came as reinforcements, following the human custom of supporting an army, to maintain the apparent system of causes.
Allah could have acted directly but chose to use means.
3
Consider Ibn Abbas' statement
Ibn Abbas distinguishes between actual fighting (only at Badr) and attending (in every later battle to increase Muslim numbers).
This clarifies that angelic presence is not limited to Badr.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Allah's use of angels teaches us that divine power does not negate the importance of means and causes in the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?
Ibn Abbas said angels only fought at Badr, yet they attend every battle to increase numbers. Are you aware of the spiritual reinforcement surrounding you even when you cannot see it? How will you remind yourself of this reality tomorrow morning?
