Avoid Envy and Honor the Companions
Author warns against envy when discussing disputes and quotes hadith about respecting Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why envy is prohibited when discussing disputes among the Companions, and the severe warning against harming or reviling them.

Core Idea
Envy in Companions' disputes leads to harm; harming them is like harming the Prophet.

This passage addresses a sensitive topic: the disagreements that occurred among the Companions. The author begins by commanding the reader to avoid envy, which can cloud judgment and lead to partisanship. He then reinforces this with a powerful hadith that equates harming a Companion with harming the Prophet himself, thereby prohibiting any form of disrespect.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prohibition of envy
Read the opening command 'Avoid the disease of envy' and notice that it is an obligation. Reflect on why envy is especially dangerous when discussing Companions' disputes.
Envy here is not just jealousy but any bias that leads to unfairness.
2
Analyze the grammatical construction
The author explains the phrase 'disease of envy' (dā' al-ḥasad). He provides two possible interpretations: envy itself as a spiritual disease, or envy compared to a physical disease. Understand the nuance.
This shows the depth of scholarly commentary.
3
Study the hadith about the Companions
Read the hadith carefully: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions...' Notice the chain of harm—from Companion to Prophet to Allah—and the threat of punishment.
The phrase 'harmed Allah' is metaphorical, meaning transgressed His limits.
4
Reflect on the consequences
Consider the severe consequences: those who harm or revile Companions incur divine punishment and curse. Relate this back to the initial warning against envy.
This underscores the sanctity of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واجْتَنِبْ دَاءَ الحَسَدٌ) أي : واترك وجوباً في حال خوضك فيما شجر الحسد، فالإضافة للبيان إن أريد الداء المعنوي، أو الحسد الشبيه بالداء، فالإضافة من إضافة المشبه به للمشبه إن أُريد الداء الحسي، والمراد داء الحسد الحامل على الميل مع أحد الطرفين على وجه غير مرضي وقد قال : «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غَرَضاً بعدي مَنْ آذاهم فقد آذاني، ومَنْ آذاني فقد آذى الله ، ومَنْ آذى الله يُوشك أن يأخذَهُ» أي: اتقوا الله ثم اتقوا الله، أو أنشدكم ثم أنشدكم الله في حق أصحابي وتعظيمهم لا تتخذوهم كالغَرَض الذي يُرمى إليه ،بالسهام فترموهم بالكلمات التي لا تناسب مقامهم، فمن آذاهم فقد آذاني، ومن آذاني فقد آذى الله ؛ أي: تعدى حدودَهُ ،وخالَفَهُ، ففيه مُشاكلةٌ، وإلا فحقيقة الإيذاء على الله محالة، آذى الله يُوشك أن يأخذَهُ ؛ أي: يقرب أن يعذبه . وفي رواية: «لا تسبوا أصحابي، مَنْ سبَّ أصحابي فعليه لعنة الله والملائكة
His saying: 'And avoid the disease of envy' means: and leave it as an obligation while you are delving into what occurred of envy. The addition [of 'disease'] is for clarification if the spiritual disease is intended, or envy similar to a disease, so the addition is of the likened to the likened if the physical disease is intended. And what is meant is the disease of envy that leads to siding with one of the two parties in an objectionable manner. And he [the Prophet] said: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions! Do not take them as targets after me. Whoever harms them has harmed me, and whoever harms me has harmed Allah, and whoever harms Allah, He is about to seize him.' That is: fear Allah, then fear Allah, or I implore you by Allah regarding my Companions and honoring them. Do not take them as a target that is shot at with arrows, thus shooting them with words that are not befitting their status. So whoever harms them has harmed me, and whoever harms me has harmed Allah; i.e., transgressed His limits and disobeyed Him. There is a similarity [in expression], for the reality of harming Allah is impossible. 'He is about to seize him' means He is about to punish him. And in another narration: 'Do not revile my Companions; whoever reviles my Companions, upon him is the curse of Allah and the angels.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage warns against the disease of envy (hasad) when discussing the disputes among the Companions. The author explains that the command to avoid envy is obligatory for those who delve into these matters. He analyzes the grammatical construction, noting that 'disease' may refer to the spiritual ailment of envy itself. The intended meaning is the envy that leads to bias towards one party in an objectionable way. Then the author quotes a hadith emphasizing the sanctity of the Companions: the Prophet warns not to make them targets of criticism. Harming them is equated with harming the Prophet and, by extension, harming Allah (a metaphorical expression). Anyone who harms the Companions is threatened with divine punishment. Another narration adds that reviling the Companions incurs the curse of Allah and the angels.

Key Terms
الحسد
أصحابي
الإيذاء
اللعنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Envy here is just ordinary jealousy between people.
Correction: In this context, envy refers to harboring ill feelings or bias that leads to unjustly criticizing or harming the Companions, not just personal jealousy.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of harming the Companions according to the hadith quoted?
A) Nothing
B) It harms the Prophet
C) It harms Allah
D) Both B and C, with the threat of punishment

Key Takeaway
Envy in discussing Companions' disputes is forbidden, and harming or reviling them invites severe divine punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about disputes among the Companions, what feeling arises in your heart? Are you free from any bias? What concrete step will you take today to ensure you do not side unjustly with any party?
?
Have you ever criticized a Companion, even in private or in a 'scholarly' discussion? How does this lesson—that harming them is like harming the Prophet—change your view? Will you repent from that speech?
?
The Prophet warned that those who harm the Companions are about to be seized by Allah. Do you truly honor the Companions in your daily speech and thoughts? What specific change will you make to show greater respect for them starting now?

Refuting Arguments Against Karamat
Refutes two arguments against karamat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main arguments used to deny karamat and how the Ash'ari tradition refutes them.

Core Idea
Karamat do not confuse saints with prophets because prophethood requires a claim.

This lesson addresses the arguments of those who deny the possibility of karamat (miracles of saints). The author presents two objections and their refutations, clarifying the distinction between prophetic miracles and saintly miracles. You will see how reason and tradition together defend the reality of karamat.

Guided Path
1
Read the directive to reject deniers
Read the opening command to discard the speech of those who deny karamat, noting the examples given.
The author includes a grammatical note about the hamza.
2
Identify the first argument and refutation
Find the argument that karamat would cause confusion with prophecy and see how the text refutes it by the claim of prophethood.
3
Identify the second argument and refutation
Find the argument that frequent karamat would cease to be extraordinary and see how the text refutes it by asserting that a breach of custom remains extraordinary.
4
Summarize the two refutations
Write a one-sentence summary for each refutation in your own words.
This helps consolidate the key points.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَمَنْ نَفَاهَا فَانْبِذَنْ كَلامَهُ :أي: ومن نفى الكرامة، وقال بعدم جوازها كالأستاذ أبي عبد الله الحليمي من أهل السنة وجمهور المعتزلة اطرحن كلامه ولا تعول عليه. وأتى المصنف بهمزة الوصل للضرورة، فتكون مكسورة، وليست همزة قطع كما قد يتوهم؛ فإن الذي في القرآن ثلاثي قال تعالى: وَقَائِي إِلَيْهِمْ [الأنفال : ٥٨] . وتمسك من نفى الكرامة بأنه لو ظهرت الخوارق من الأولياء لالتبس النبي بغيره ؛ لأن الخارق إنما هو المعجزة، وبأنها لو ظهرت على أيديهم لكثرت بكثرتهم وخرجت عن كونها خارقة للعادة والفرض أنها كذلك، ورُدَّ الأول بأنه ليس في وقوعها التباسُ النبي بغيره للفرق بين المعجزة والكرامة، بدعوى النبوة في الأولى وعدمها في الثانية، ورُدَّ الثاني بأنا لا نُسلّم أنها تخرج بكثرتها عن كونها خارقة للعادة، بل غاية الأمر استمرار خرق العادة وذلك لا يوجب كونه عادة . وسئل بعضهم : لأي شيءٍ كثرت الكرامات في الزمان المتأخر عن الزمان المتقدم؟ فأجاب بأن ذلك لضعف اعتقاد المتأخرين، فاختيج لتأليفهم بالكرامات ليعتقدوا في الصالحين، وأما المتقدمون فاعتقادهم تابع لميزان الشرع .
His statement: 'And whoever denies them, then cast aside his speech' means: Whoever denies the karama and says it is not possible, like al-Ustadh Abu Abdullah al-Halimi among the Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila, discard his speech and do not rely on it. And the author inserted a conjunctive hamza out of necessity, so it is kasra, and it is not a hamza qat' as might be imagined; for what is in the Quran is triliteral: He said, 'And I will convey to them' [Al-Anfal: 58]. And those who deny karama adhered to [the argument] that if extraordinary things appeared from the saints, the prophet would be confused with others, because the extraordinary is only the miracle; and that if they appeared at their hands, they would become numerous due to their numbers and would cease to be extraordinary while it is assumed that they are. The first [argument] is refuted by [saying] that there is no confusion of the prophet with others in their occurrence because of the difference between the miracle and the karama, by the claim of prophethood in the former and its absence in the latter. The second is refuted by [saying] we do not concede that they cease to be extraordinary by their multiplicity; rather, the utmost is a continuation of breaking the custom, and that does not necessitate it becoming customary. And some were asked: Why did karamat become more numerous in the later time than the earlier time? He answered: That is due to the weakness of the belief of the later ones, so they needed to be influenced by karamat so that they would believe in the righteous; as for the earlier ones, their belief was according to the scale of the Law.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage treats the subject of those who deny the possibility of karamat (miracles of saints). It begins by explaining the verse 'وَمَنْ نَفَاهَا فَانْبِذَنْ كَلامَهُ' (whoever denies them, cast aside his speech) as referring to those like Abu Abdullah al-Halimi from the Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila who deny the permissibility of karamat. The author then makes a grammatical note about the hamza in the verb 'فَانْبِذَنْ' being a conjunctive hamza (hamzat wasl), not a cut hamza (hamzat qat'), citing Quranic evidence. Two arguments of the deniers are presented: first, that if extraordinary events appeared from saints, it would cause confusion with prophets since only prophets have miracles; second, that if such events occurred frequently from many saints, they would no longer be extraordinary. These are refuted: the first refutation points out that karamat do not cause confusion because the prophet claims prophethood while the saint does not; the second refutation argues that frequency does not negate the breaking of custom, as a continual breach of norm does not become a norm. Finally, an additional question about why karamat are more numerous in later times is answered by saying that later believers have weaker faith and need such signs to strengthen their belief, while early believers relied directly on the Sharia.

Key Terms
كرامة
معجزة
خارق للعادة
أبو عبد الله الحليمي
همزة الوصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karamat confuse saints with prophets because both involve extraordinary events.
Correction: The text clarifies that the distinction lies in the claim of prophethood: prophets claim it, saints do not, so no confusion arises.

Checkpoint
How does the text refute the argument that karamat would cause confusion with prophethood?
A) By saying that saints are infallible like prophets.
B) By stating that a karama is claimed as a prophetic miracle.
C) By noting that the prophet claims prophethood while the saint does not.
D) By denying that karamat are extraordinary.

Key Takeaway
Karamat are distinct from miracles because saints do not claim prophethood, and their frequency does not diminish their extraordinary nature.

?

?
The deniers feared confusion between prophets and saints. In your own heart, do you equate spiritual power or experiences with authority? Are you more impressed by extraordinary signs than by the truth of a person's message? What does this reveal about your own faith?
?

The Wisdom Behind Increased Karamat in Later Times
Answers why karamat are more frequent in later times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why karamat were more frequent in later Islamic history according to this text.

Core Idea
Later believers needed karamat due to weak faith; earlier ones relied on Sharia.

This lesson examines a question about the increased occurrence of karamat in later times. The answer provides insight into the pedagogical role of miracles for strengthening faith. It contrasts the strong faith of early Muslims with the weaker faith of later generations.

Guided Path
1
Read the question about increased karamat
Read the question asking why karamat became more numerous in later times.
2
Identify the answer about weak faith
Find the explanation that later believers had weaker faith and needed karamat to strengthen their belief.
3
Contrast with early believers
Notice that early believers relied directly on the Sharia, not on extraordinary signs.
This highlights the different spiritual contexts.

قوله : (وَمَنْ نَفَاهَا فَانْبِذَنْ كَلامَهُ :أي: ومن نفى الكرامة، وقال بعدم جوازها كالأستاذ أبي عبد الله الحليمي من أهل السنة وجمهور المعتزلة اطرحن كلامه ولا تعول عليه. وأتى المصنف بهمزة الوصل للضرورة، فتكون مكسورة، وليست همزة قطع كما قد يتوهم؛ فإن الذي في القرآن ثلاثي قال تعالى: وَقَائِي إِلَيْهِمْ [الأنفال : ٥٨] . وتمسك من نفى الكرامة بأنه لو ظهرت الخوارق من الأولياء لالتبس النبي بغيره ؛ لأن الخارق إنما هو المعجزة، وبأنها لو ظهرت على أيديهم لكثرت بكثرتهم وخرجت عن كونها خارقة للعادة والفرض أنها كذلك، ورُدَّ الأول بأنه ليس في وقوعها التباسُ النبي بغيره للفرق بين المعجزة والكرامة، بدعوى النبوة في الأولى وعدمها في الثانية، ورُدَّ الثاني بأنا لا نُسلّم أنها تخرج بكثرتها عن كونها خارقة للعادة، بل غاية الأمر استمرار خرق العادة وذلك لا يوجب كونه عادة . وسئل بعضهم : لأي شيءٍ كثرت الكرامات في الزمان المتأخر عن الزمان المتقدم؟ فأجاب بأن ذلك لضعف اعتقاد المتأخرين، فاختيج لتأليفهم بالكرامات ليعتقدوا في الصالحين، وأما المتقدمون فاعتقادهم تابع لميزان الشرع .
His statement: 'And whoever denies them, then cast aside his speech' means: Whoever denies the karama and says it is not possible, like al-Ustadh Abu Abdullah al-Halimi among the Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila, discard his speech and do not rely on it. And the author inserted a conjunctive hamza out of necessity, so it is kasra, and it is not a hamza qat' as might be imagined; for what is in the Quran is triliteral: He said, 'And I will convey to them' [Al-Anfal: 58]. And those who deny karama adhered to [the argument] that if extraordinary things appeared from the saints, the prophet would be confused with others, because the extraordinary is only the miracle; and that if they appeared at their hands, they would become numerous due to their numbers and would cease to be extraordinary while it is assumed that they are. The first [argument] is refuted by [saying] that there is no confusion of the prophet with others in their occurrence because of the difference between the miracle and the karama, by the claim of prophethood in the former and its absence in the latter. The second is refuted by [saying] we do not concede that they cease to be extraordinary by their multiplicity; rather, the utmost is a continuation of breaking the custom, and that does not necessitate it becoming customary. And some were asked: Why did karamat become more numerous in the later time than the earlier time? He answered: That is due to the weakness of the belief of the later ones, so they needed to be influenced by karamat so that they would believe in the righteous; as for the earlier ones, their belief was according to the scale of the Law.

Supplication and Its Effect on Divine Decree
Commentary on supplication's benefit and its relation to two types of decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how supplication benefits the living and the dead according to Ahl al-Sunna, and how it interacts with the irrevocable and conditional decrees.

Core Idea
Supplication does not cancel destiny but transforms harm into grace.

This lesson examines a key passage from Tuhfat al-Mureed that explains the benefit of supplication (du'a) according to Sunni theology. The commentator addresses whether supplication can change divine decrees, distinguishing between irrevocable and conditional decrees, and clarifies a potential misunderstanding from the Quran. By the end, you'll see how supplication is both effective and consistent with qadar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage silently, then its English translation. Let the commentator's own flow shape your first impression.
Pay attention to the hadith and Quranic verse cited.
2
Identify the definition and scope of supplication
Note how supplication is defined as humble asking or raising needs to Allah. The commentator asserts it benefits both living and dead, and even from a disbeliever under oppression.
3
Understand the Quranic clarification
The commentator explains that the verse 'The supplication of the disbelievers is but in error' refers specifically to their plea for relief from Hellfire on Judgment Day, not to all supplications.
This resolves an apparent contradiction.
4
Distinguish between irrevocable and conditional decree
The passage divides decree into two types. For the conditional, supplication can change it directly. For the irrevocable, supplication does not lift it but Allah sends grace (lutf) that mitigates the harm.
Example: a falling rock turned into sand.
5
Reflect on the role of divine grace
Consider how this understanding balances divine sovereignty with human agency. Supplication is a means through which Allah's mercy operates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات [ القسم الثالثُ : السَّمعيات الدعاء شروطه وآدابه ٨٤ - وعِنْدَنَا أَنَّ الدُّعَاءَ يَنْفَعُ كَما مِنَ القُرْآنِ وَعْداً يُسْمَعُ قوله : وعِنْدَنَا أَنَّ الدُّعَاءَ يَنْفَعُ) أي : وعندنا معاشر أهل السنة أن الدعاء الذي هو الطلب على سبيل التضرع، وقيل: هو رفع الحاجات إلى رافع الدرجات ينفع الأحياء والأموات إن دعوت لهم، ويضرهم إن دعوت عليهم، وإن صدر من كافر على الراجح، لحديث أنس رضي الله عنه : دعوة المظلوم مُستجابةٌ ولو كافراً (۱) ، وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا دُعَاهُ الْكَفِرِينَ إِلَّا فِي ضَلَلِ [الرعد: ١٤] فمعناه أنه لا يُستجاب لهم في خصوص الدعاء بتخفيف عذاب جهنم عنهم يوم القيامة، وروى الحاكم وصححه : أنه قال : لا يعني حَذَرٌ من قَدَرٍ ، والدعاء ينفع ممَّا نزل وممَّا لم ينزل، وإن البلاء لينزل ويتلقاه الدعاء فيتعالجان إلى يوم القيامة (٢) . والدعاء ينفع في القضاء المُبرم والقضاء المُعلَّق : أما الثاني فلا استحالة في رفع ما عُلّق رفعه منه على الدعاء، ولا في نزول ما عُلِّق نزوله منه على الدعاء. وأما الأول فالدعاء وإن لم يرفعه لكن الله تعالى يُنزل لطفه بالداعي، كما إذا قضى عليه قضاءٌ مُبرماً بأن ينزل عليه صخرةٌ، فإذا دعا الله تعالى حصل له اللطف، بأن تصير الصخرة مفتتة كالرمل وتنزل عليه وانقسام القضاء إلى مُبرم ومُعلَّق ظاهر بحسب اللوح
The Audible Matters. [The third section: The Audible Matters – Supplication, its conditions and etiquettes. 84 – And with us that supplication benefits, as from the Qur'an a promise is heard. His saying: 'And with us that supplication benefits' means: With us, the community of Ahl al-Sunna, that supplication (du'a'), which is asking in a manner of humility, and it is said: it is raising needs to the Raiser of degrees, benefits the living and the dead if you pray for them, and harms them if you pray against them, even if it comes from a disbeliever according to the preponderant opinion, due to the hadith of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him): 'The supplication of the oppressed is answered even if he is a disbeliever.' As for His statement (Exalted): 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is but in error' [al-Ra'd: 14], its meaning is that it is not answered for them specifically regarding the supplication for alleviating the punishment of Hell from them on the Day of Resurrection. And al-Hakim narrated and authenticated that he said: 'Precaution does not avail against destiny, and supplication benefits against what has descended and what has not descended, and indeed affliction descends and supplication meets it and they grapple until the Day of Resurrection.' And supplication benefits in the irrevocable decree (al-qada' al-mubram) and the conditional decree (al-qada' al-mu'allaq). As for the second, there is no impossibility in the lifting of what was suspended on the condition of supplication, nor in the descent of what was suspended on the condition of supplication. As for the first, supplication does not lift it, but Allah (Exalted) sends His grace to the supplicant, as when an irrevocable decree is passed upon him that a rock will fall on him, so if he supplicates to Allah, grace occurs for him, such that the rock becomes crumbled like sand and falls upon him. And the division of decree (qada') into irrevocable and conditional is apparent according to the Preserved Tablet.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of al-Jawhara: 'And with us that supplication benefits, as from the Qur'an a promise is heard.' The commentator first defines supplication (du'a') as humble asking or raising needs to Allah. He states that according to Ahl al-Sunna, supplication benefits both the living and the dead—if one prays for them, it benefits, and if one prays against them, it harms. This holds true even if the supplicant is a disbeliever, based on the hadith that the oppressed person's supplication is answered even if the oppressor is a disbeliever. The commentator then addresses the verse 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is but in error' (al-Ra'd:14), explaining that it refers specifically to their supplication for relief from Hellfire on the Day of Resurrection, not to supplication in general. Next, he cites a hadith (narrated by al-Hakim) that precaution does not avert destiny, but supplication benefits against both what has already descended (affliction) and what has not yet descended, and that affliction and supplication grapple until the Day of Resurrection. Finally, he distinguishes between two types of decree: the irrevocable decree (al-qada' al-mubram) and the conditional decree (al-qada' al-mu'allaq). For the conditional decree, there is no problem in the decree being lifted or brought about by supplication since it was conditioned upon it. For the irrevocable decree, supplication does not lift it, but Allah grants grace (lutf) to the supplicant, such that the harm is mitigated, exemplified by a rock that would have crushed a person being turned into sand. The division of decree into these two types is evident from the Preserved Tablet.

Key Terms
الدعاء
القضاء المبرم
القضاء المعلق
اللطف
اللوح المحفوظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that supplication cannot change any divine decree, or that it contradicts qadar.
Correction: Supplication does not contradict qadar; it is part of the means through which Allah decrees outcomes. For conditional decrees, supplication is the condition; for irrevocable decrees, supplication brings divine grace that mitigates harm.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does supplication affect the irrevocable decree (al-qada' al-mubram)?
A) It cancels the decree entirely.
B) It does not affect it at all.
C) It does not lift it, but Allah grants grace to ease the harm.
D) It makes the decree conditional and thus changeable.

Key Takeaway
Supplication is a powerful means that works within divine decree: it changes conditional decrees and draws Allah's grace in irrevocable ones, affirming both human agency and divine sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial that seems irreversible, do you still call upon Allah with genuine hope that His grace can transform it? Or does despair creep in because you feel your supplication is futile? How does this teaching challenge that despair?
?
How does the distinction between conditional and irrevocable decree affect the way you supplicate? Will you now pray more intensely even for things that seem fixed, knowing that du'a invites divine grace?
?
The passage states that even a disbeliever's supplication can be answered. What does this tell you about Allah's mercy? Do you sometimes hold back from supplication because you feel unworthy, and how does this teaching refute that?

The Sunni Doctrine That Supplication Benefits
Author affirms Sunni view on dua with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that dua benefits the living and the dead, including disbelievers, and how the Quranic verse is interpreted.

Core Idea
Supplication benefits everyone, even disbelievers, by God's promise.

This lesson establishes the core Sunni belief that supplication (dua) is effective and beneficial, contrary to some who deny its benefit. The author cites a hadith and interprets a Quranic verse to support this view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style.
2
Identify the main claims
The passage asserts that dua benefits the living and dead, and even disbelievers. Find the hadith that supports this.
3
Understand the Quranic interpretation
The author explains a verse that seems to contradict this view. Understand how he limits its meaning to the afterlife.
This resolves an apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندنا أن الدعاء ينفع كما من القرآن وعداً يسمع
قوله : وعندنا أن الدعاء ينفع) أي : وعندنا معاشر أهل السنة أن الدعاء الذي هو الطلب على سبيل التضرع، وقيل: هو رفع الحاجات إلى رافع الدرجات ينفع الأحياء والأموات إن دعوت لهم، ويضرهم إن دعوت عليهم، وإن صدر من كافر على الراجح، لحديث أنس رضي الله عنه : دعوة المظلوم مستجابة ولو كافراً، وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا دُعَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ إِلَّا فِي ضَلَالٍ﴾ فمعناه أنه لا يستجاب لهم في خصوص الدعاء بتخفيف عذاب جهنم عنهم يوم القيامة، وروى الحاكم وصححه : أنه قال : لا يعجز حذر من قدر، والدعاء ينفع مما نزل ومما لم ينزل، وإن البلاء لينزل ويتلقاه الدعاء فيتعالجان إلى يوم القيامة.
والدعاء ينفع في القضاء المبرم والقضاء المعلق :
أما الثاني فلا استحالة في رفع ما علق رفعه منه على الدعاء، ولا في نزول ما علق نزوله منه على الدعاء.
وأما الأول فالدعاء وإن لم يرفعه لكن الله تعالى ينزل لطفه بالداعي، كما إذا قضى عليه قضاء مبرماً بأن ينزل عليه صخرة، فإذا دعا الله تعالى حصل له اللطف، بأن تصير الصخرة مفتتة كالرمل وتنزل عليه وانقسام القضاء إلى مبرم ومعلق ظاهر بحسب اللوح المحفوظ، وأما بحسب العلم فجميع الأشياء مبرمة؛ لأنه إن علم الله حصول المعلق عليه حصل المعلق ولا بد، وإن علم الله عدم حصوله، لم يحصل ولا بد، لكن لا يترك الشخص الدعاء اتكالاً على ذلك كما لا يترك الأكل اتكالاً على إبرام الله الأمر في الشبع.
وأما عند المعتزلة فالدعاء لا ينفع، ولا يكفرون بذلك؛ لأنهم لم يكذبوا القرآن كقوله تعالى : ادْعُونِي أَسْتَجِبْ لَكُمْ، بل أولوا الدعاء بالعبادة، والإجابة بالثواب.
And with us, that supplication benefits, as from the Qur'an a promise is heard. His saying: 'And with us that supplication benefits' – meaning: And with us, the community of Ahl al-Sunna, that supplication, which is requesting in a humble manner, and it is said: it is raising needs to the Raiser of degrees, benefits the living and the dead if you pray for them, and harms them if you pray against them, and even if it issues from a disbeliever according to the preponderant view, due to the hadith of Anas, may God be pleased with him: 'The supplication of the oppressed is answered even if he is a disbeliever.' As for His statement, exalted: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is only in error' – its meaning is that it is not answered for them specifically in the supplication for alleviating the punishment of Hell from them on the Day of Resurrection. And al-Hakim narrated and authenticated that he said: 'Caution does not avert destiny, and supplication benefits against what has descended and what has not descended, and indeed affliction descends and supplication meets it and they grapple until the Day of Resurrection.' And supplication benefits in the determined decree (al-qada' al-mubram) and the conditional decree (al-qada' al-mu'allaq): As for the second, there is no impossibility in removing what has been made conditional on its removal upon supplication, nor in the descent of what has been made conditional on its descent upon supplication. As for the first, supplication – even if it does not remove it – but God, exalted, sends down His kindness to the one who supplicates, just as if a determined decree has been decreed upon him that a rock will fall on him, then if he supplicates, God, exalted, grants him kindness, such that the rock becomes crumbled like sand and falls upon him. And the division of decree into determined and conditional is apparent according to the Preserved Tablet, but according to knowledge, all things are determined; because if God knows the occurrence of the conditional, the conditional occurs necessarily, and if God knows its non-occurrence, it does not occur necessarily, but the person does not abandon supplication relying on that, just as he does not abandon eating relying on God's determination of the matter of satiety. And as for the Mu'tazila, supplication does not benefit, but they are not disbelieved on account of that, because they did not deny the Qur'an, such as His statement: 'Call upon Me, I will answer you,' rather they interpret 'supplication' as worship, and 'response' as reward.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and refutation. It begins by affirming the Sunni position that supplication (dua) benefits the living and the dead, and even a disbeliever's dua is answered in worldly matters, citing a hadith. It then explains a Quranic verse that seems to deny the answer of disbelievers' dua, limiting it to the afterlife. The author next distinguishes between two types of divine decrees: the determined (mubram) and the conditional (mu'allaq). For conditional decrees, dua can directly cause change. For determined decrees, dua does not change the decree but brings divine kindness that mitigates harm, using the example of a falling rock turning to sand. The division is explained as apparent from the Preserved Tablet but all things are ultimately determined in God's knowledge, yet one should not abandon dua any more than eating for satiety. Finally, the Mu'tazila are mentioned as denying the benefit of dua, but they are not declared disbelievers because they interpret the relevant Quranic verses metaphorically (dua as worship, response as reward).

Key Terms
دعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dua from a disbeliever is never answered.
Correction: The author clarifies that dua from a disbeliever is answered in worldly matters, based on a hadith, and the Quranic verse refers only to the afterlife.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Quranic verse 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is only in error' mean?
A) It means their dua is never answered at all.
B) It is limited to dua for alleviating Hellfire punishment on the Day of Resurrection.
C) It means they worship idols.
D) It means their dua is only for worldly things.

Key Takeaway
Dua benefits all, including disbelievers in worldly matters, and the Quranic verse is specific to the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah answers even the supplication of an oppressed disbeliever, how much more does He hear your cries when you feel undeserving? Will you now make dua with greater confidence and urgency, knowing that your worthiness is not the measure?
?
The lesson warns that supplication can harm if prayed against another. Reflect on a time you may have prayed against someone in anger. Knowing the power of your words, what will you do to seek forgiveness and change your heart?
?
Dua benefits against affliction that has already descended and that which has not yet come. Are you using dua as a daily shield, or only as a last resort? What specific situation in your life right now can you actively cover with dua starting today?

Supplication and the Two Types of Divine Decree
Author explains dua's effect on determined and conditional decrees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between determined and conditional decrees and how supplication affects each, as well as the Mu'tazila view.

Core Idea
Dua changes conditional decrees and brings kindness in determined decrees.

This lesson delves into the types of divine decrees and how supplication interacts with them. It also addresses the Mu'tazila position that denies the benefit of dua.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of decree
The passage distinguishes between the determined decree (al-qada' al-mubram) and the conditional decree (al-qada' al-mu'allaq). Understand their definitions.
Notice the author's example of a falling rock.
2
Understand how dua affects each
For conditional decrees, dua can directly cause change. For determined decrees, dua does not remove the decree but brings God's kindness (lutf) to mitigate it.
Consider why this distinction matters for theology.
3
Note the Mu'tazila view
The Mu'tazila deny that dua benefits, but they are not declared disbelievers because they reinterpret relevant Quranic verses metaphorically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندنا أن الدعاء ينفع كما من القرآن وعداً يسمع
قوله : وعندنا أن الدعاء ينفع) أي : وعندنا معاشر أهل السنة أن الدعاء الذي هو الطلب على سبيل التضرع، وقيل: هو رفع الحاجات إلى رافع الدرجات ينفع الأحياء والأموات إن دعوت لهم، ويضرهم إن دعوت عليهم، وإن صدر من كافر على الراجح، لحديث أنس رضي الله عنه : دعوة المظلوم مستجابة ولو كافراً، وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا دُعَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ إِلَّا فِي ضَلَالٍ﴾ فمعناه أنه لا يستجاب لهم في خصوص الدعاء بتخفيف عذاب جهنم عنهم يوم القيامة، وروى الحاكم وصححه : أنه قال : لا يعجز حذر من قدر، والدعاء ينفع مما نزل ومما لم ينزل، وإن البلاء لينزل ويتلقاه الدعاء فيتعالجان إلى يوم القيامة.
والدعاء ينفع في القضاء المبرم والقضاء المعلق :
أما الثاني فلا استحالة في رفع ما علق رفعه منه على الدعاء، ولا في نزول ما علق نزوله منه على الدعاء.
وأما الأول فالدعاء وإن لم يرفعه لكن الله تعالى ينزل لطفه بالداعي، كما إذا قضى عليه قضاء مبرماً بأن ينزل عليه صخرة، فإذا دعا الله تعالى حصل له اللطف، بأن تصير الصخرة مفتتة كالرمل وتنزل عليه وانقسام القضاء إلى مبرم ومعلق ظاهر بحسب اللوح المحفوظ، وأما بحسب العلم فجميع الأشياء مبرمة؛ لأنه إن علم الله حصول المعلق عليه حصل المعلق ولا بد، وإن علم الله عدم حصوله، لم يحصل ولا بد، لكن لا يترك الشخص الدعاء اتكالاً على ذلك كما لا يترك الأكل اتكالاً على إبرام الله الأمر في الشبع.
وأما عند المعتزلة فالدعاء لا ينفع، ولا يكفرون بذلك؛ لأنهم لم يكذبوا القرآن كقوله تعالى : ادْعُونِي أَسْتَجِبْ لَكُمْ، بل أولوا الدعاء بالعبادة، والإجابة بالثواب.
And with us, that supplication benefits, as from the Qur'an a promise is heard. His saying: 'And with us that supplication benefits' – meaning: And with us, the community of Ahl al-Sunna, that supplication, which is requesting in a humble manner, and it is said: it is raising needs to the Raiser of degrees, benefits the living and the dead if you pray for them, and harms them if you pray against them, and even if it issues from a disbeliever according to the preponderant view, due to the hadith of Anas, may God be pleased with him: 'The supplication of the oppressed is answered even if he is a disbeliever.' As for His statement, exalted: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is only in error' – its meaning is that it is not answered for them specifically in the supplication for alleviating the punishment of Hell from them on the Day of Resurrection. And al-Hakim narrated and authenticated that he said: 'Caution does not avert destiny, and supplication benefits against what has descended and what has not descended, and indeed affliction descends and supplication meets it and they grapple until the Day of Resurrection.' And supplication benefits in the determined decree (al-qada' al-mubram) and the conditional decree (al-qada' al-mu'allaq): As for the second, there is no impossibility in removing what has been made conditional on its removal upon supplication, nor in the descent of what has been made conditional on its descent upon supplication. As for the first, supplication – even if it does not remove it – but God, exalted, sends down His kindness to the one who supplicates, just as if a determined decree has been decreed upon him that a rock will fall on him, then if he supplicates, God, exalted, grants him kindness, such that the rock becomes crumbled like sand and falls upon him. And the division of decree into determined and conditional is apparent according to the Preserved Tablet, but according to knowledge, all things are determined; because if God knows the occurrence of the conditional, the conditional occurs necessarily, and if God knows its non-occurrence, it does not occur necessarily, but the person does not abandon supplication relying on that, just as he does not abandon eating relying on God's determination of the matter of satiety. And as for the Mu'tazila, supplication does not benefit, but they are not disbelieved on account of that, because they did not deny the Qur'an, such as His statement: 'Call upon Me, I will answer you,' rather they interpret 'supplication' as worship, and 'response' as reward.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and refutation. It begins by affirming the Sunni position that supplication (dua) benefits the living and the dead, and even a disbeliever's dua is answered in worldly matters, citing a hadith. It then explains a Quranic verse that seems to deny the answer of disbelievers' dua, limiting it to the afterlife. The author next distinguishes between two types of divine decrees: the determined (mubram) and the conditional (mu'allaq). For conditional decrees, dua can directly cause change. For determined decrees, dua does not change the decree but brings divine kindness that mitigates harm, using the example of a falling rock turning to sand. The division is explained as apparent from the Preserved Tablet but all things are ultimately determined in God's knowledge, yet one should not abandon dua any more than eating for satiety. Finally, the Mu'tazila are mentioned as denying the benefit of dua, but they are not declared disbelievers because they interpret the relevant Quranic verses metaphorically (dua as worship, response as reward).

Key Terms
قضاء مبرم
قضاء معلق
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dua cannot change anything in destiny.
Correction: The author explains that dua affects conditional decrees and for determined decrees brings divine kindness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens when a determined decree of a rock falling is met with supplication?
A) The rock stops.
B) The rock becomes crumbled like sand.
C) Nothing happens.
D) The decree is canceled.

Key Takeaway
Dua is effective: it can change conditional decrees and for determined decrees, God sends kindness to lighten the outcome.

Conditions of Supplication
Conditions for effective supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key conditions that must be fulfilled for a supplication to be valid and effective.

Core Idea
Supplication has prerequisites; without them, it may not be accepted.

Before making du'a, one must ensure certain inner and outer prerequisites are met. The author lists conditions that concern the person's state, the content of the request, and the attitude towards Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditions passage
Read the Arabic passage listing the conditions of supplication. Notice the pattern: each condition is introduced with 'An' or 'Alla'.
The passage begins with 'فمن شروطه'.
2
Identify each condition
List the conditions mentioned: lawful sustenance, certainty of response, attentive heart, avoiding sin/severance/wasting rights, avoiding supplication for the impossible.
There are five conditions.
3
Understand the rationale
For each condition, consider why it is necessary. For example, lawful food ensures the person is spiritually pure.
The last condition is explained: asking the impossible resembles bad manners towards Allah's power.
4
Reflect on the last condition
The prohibition of asking for the impossible even habitually is tied to adab (manners) towards Allah. Reflect on how this affects your du'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن للدعاء شروطاً وآداباً :
فمن شروطه أكل الحلال، وأن يدعو وهو موقن بالإجابة، وألا يكون قلبه غافلاً، وألا يدعو بما فيه إثم أو قطيعة رحم، أو إضاعة حقوق المسلمين، وألا يدعو بمحال ولو عادة؛ لأن الدعاء به يشبه التحكم على القدرة القاضية بدوامها، وذلك إساءة أدب على الله تعالى.
ومن آدابه : أن يتحرى الأوقات الفاضلة، كأن يدعو في السجود، وعند الأذان والإقامة، ومنها : تقديم الوضوء والصلاة، واستقبال القبلة، ورفع الأيدي إلى جهة السماء، وتقديم التوبة، والاعتراف بالذنب والإخلاص، وافتتاحه بالحمد والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وختمه بها، وجعلها في وسطه أيضاً.
And know that supplication has conditions and etiquettes: Among its conditions: consuming lawful sustenance, supplicating while being certain of the response, that his heart not be heedless, that he not supplicate for something containing sin, severing of kinship, or wasting the rights of Muslims, and that he not supplicate for something impossible even habitually, because supplicating for it resembles arbitrariness towards the omnipotent power in its perpetuity, and that is bad manners towards God, exalted. And among its etiquettes: that he seek out virtuous times, such as supplicating in prostration, and at the call to prayer (adhan) and the commencement (iqama), and among them: performing ablution and prayer beforehand, facing the qibla, raising hands towards the sky, preceding with repentance, acknowledgment of sin, sincerity, opening supplication with praise and blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and concluding with it, and also including it in the middle.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration. It first lists the conditions (shurut) of supplication: lawful food, certainty of response, attentiveness of heart, avoiding supplication for sin or family severance or wasting Muslim rights, and avoiding supplication for the impossible habitually (because it implies bad manners towards God's perpetual power). Then it lists the etiquettes (adab): choosing virtuous times (prostration, adhan, iqama), performing ablution and prayer, facing qibla, raising hands, preceding repentance, acknowledgment of sin, sincerity, and opening and closing with praise and blessings on the Prophet, also including it in the middle.

Key Terms
شروط
دعاء
حلال
إجابة
غافل
إثم
قطيعة رحم
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Supplication only depends on sincerity; external conditions like lawful food do not matter.
Correction: The author explicitly lists consuming lawful sustenance as a condition, showing that both inner sincerity and outer purity are required.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is mentioned as a condition (shart) of supplication?
A) Raising hands towards the sky
B) Consuming lawful sustenance
C) Supplicating in prostration
D) Opening with praise of God

Key Takeaway
Supplication has five key conditions: lawful food, certainty, attentiveness, avoiding sin, and avoiding impossible requests.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly ensure your sustenance is halal before making du'a? What steps can you take today to verify the purity of your income?
?
When you supplicate, is your heart fully present, or are you reciting words mechanically? How can you cultivate certainty and attentiveness starting tonight?
?
Have you ever asked Allah for something that would harm others or cut family ties? How does this condition force you to examine your hidden desires?

Etiquettes of Supplication
Etiquettes for proper supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the recommended etiquettes that enhance the quality and acceptance of supplication.

Core Idea
Supplication has beautiful etiquettes that align the heart and body in humility before Allah.

After fulfilling the conditions, one should observe the etiquettes (adab) of du'a. These include choosing virtuous times, physical preparation, and the manner of beginning and ending the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Read the etiquettes passage
Read the Arabic passage listing the etiquettes. Note that they start with 'ومن آدابه'.
2
Categorize the etiquettes
Group the etiquettes into temporal (times), physical (ablution, facing qibla, raising hands), and verbal (repentance, praise, salawat).
There are many items, but they fall into these categories.
3
Understand the significance of each
For each etiquette, reflect on why it is recommended. For example, prostration is a state of closeness to Allah.
4
Note the structure of the du'a
The author recommends opening and closing with praise and blessings on the Prophet, and also including them in the middle.
This emphasizes the importance of praising Allah and invoking blessings.

Source Text

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Supplication can be done anytime and in any manner without special preparation.
Correction: The author lists specific times, physical actions, and verbal formulas that enhance the du'a, showing that manner and timing matter.

Checkpoint

B) Raising hands towards the sky

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you take the time to perform ablution and face the qibla, or do you treat it as a casual afterthought? What does your posture reveal about the reverence in your heart?
?
Are you quick to ask Allah for your needs but slow to begin with praise and blessings on His Prophet? How might changing that order transform your consciousness of who you are speaking to?
?
Have you ever rushed through a supplication without pausing to repent of your sins first? If you did, what might happen if you made tawba the non-negotiable first step of every du'a from now on?
